{"title": "Dividend vs. Growth: Is Keppel Ltd the New \u201cMust-Own\u201d Hybrid for Singaporeans?", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/dividend-vs-growth-keppel-ltd-033000777.html", "text": "When I began investing, I found myself confronted with the age-old question: Do I go for growth or income?\n\nWhat if I told you that there\u2019s no need to sacrifice one for the other, and there are companies that offer both?\n\nIn this article, I\u2019ll talk about how Keppel Limited (SGX: BN4), or Keppel, has undergone a major transformation in recent years, which firmly solidifies this conglomerate as both an income and growth player in the Singapore market.\n\nDividend vs Growth: Why the Trade-Off Exists\n\nThe trade-off between growth and income stocks boils down simply to a difference in priority: reinvesting for expansion (growth stocks) or income and capital stability (income stocks).\n\nA company that offers a combination of both growth and income is rare, as it requires strong and stable cash generation (to pay a steady income), alongside the availability of high-return reinvestment opportunities for growth.\n\nKeppel\u2019s Transformation: From Cyclical to Structural\n\nFirst, a short sharing on Keppel\u2019s recent transformation.\n\nKeppel has successfully shed its legacy conglomerate skin, transitioning into a lean, asset-light global manager.\n\nBy pivoting away from the highly cyclical offshore and marine sector, the group is now a specialist operator in the \u201cNew Economy\u201d trifecta: Infrastructure, Connectivity, and Real Estate.\n\nThis shift doesn\u2019t just improve margins, but it also positions Keppel at the epicentre of multi-decade tailwinds like the energy transition and the digitalisation boom.\n\nTo achieve this, the group has been divesting non-core assets, such as the recent sale of its stake in M1, to better focus on its new strategy.\n\nThe Dividend Case: Does Keppel Still Deliver Income?\n\nLet us now focus on its income potential.\n\nCurrently, Keppel offers a trailing dividend yield of almost 4%, with the group having paid a consistent annual dividend over the past five years.\n\nAt 4% dividend yield, while lower compared to traditional dividend plays like REITs (average of 5.9%) and banks (average of 5.5%), it is important to note that Keppel\u2019s S$0.47 per share for 2025 represents a stunning annual growth of 38%.\n\nFurthermore, the conglomerate\u2019s dividends are backed by increasing cash flows from operations, with an estimated payout ratio of 58.2%.\n\nGiven the group\u2019s recurring fee income generation, there\u2019s a good case for continued dividend growth.\n\nThe Growth Case: Where Upside Comes From\n\nSo, where will future growth come from for Keppel?\n\nIts asset management business is an attractive growth opportunity: as funds under management increase, Keppel earns increasing, recurring fees with high margins.\n\nBy positioning itself at the intersection of renewable infrastructure and green energy, the group is capturing high-quality earnings as the energy transition accelerates.\n\nThis growth is further amplified by Keppel\u2019s aggressive asset monetisation, including the divesting of legacy non-core holdings, freeing up dry powder for higher-yielding projects.\n\nThis move fundamentally improves the group\u2019s return on equity (ROE) and margins.\n\nFinancial Snapshot\n\nKeppel\u2019s shares currently trade at roughly S$11.93, with a one-year range between S$6.12 and S$13.25.\n\nRevenue and net profit have seen stabilisation in recent years as the group\u2019s higher-margin new initiatives are offset by the ongoing divestment of its traditional business segments.\n\nAs of 2025, infrastructure makes up the bulk of Keppel\u2019s revenue at S$4.15 billion, with real estate at S$221 million and connectivity at S$953 million.\n\nKeppel\u2019s bottom-line improvement is also gaining traction, with operating margins more than doubling from 5.7% in 2022 to 12.7% in 2025.\n\nThis has allowed the group to steadily repair its balance sheet; net debt to EBITDA improved to 5.1x as of December 2025, down from 5.9x just a year prior.\n\nInvestors should note that the group\u2019s new business segments (New Keppel) have an ROE of 18.7%, comfortably above the overall ROE of 7.2%.\n\nAs the group continues to grow its New Keppel segment and divests its lower-margin non-core operations, this figure of 7.2% should continue trending higher in the future.\n\nWhat Makes Keppel a \u201cHybrid\u201d Stock Today And Key Risks\n\nKeppel\u2019s solid dividend yield and growth, with its exposure to secular growth trends such as infrastructure, digitalisation, and renewable energy, position the group as a rare \u201chybrid\u201d stock that offers income and growth.\n\nHowever, investors should monitor for risks such as execution risk: can Keppel continue growing its new businesses while successfully shedding its traditional operations?\n\nThere\u2019s also the cyclical risk involved, given the group\u2019s exposure to real estate.\n\nFinally, there\u2019s also a valuation risk to consider.\n\nValuation: Is the Hybrid Story Already Priced In?\n\nKeppel is currently priced for perfection, trading at 2.1x book and roughly 20.8x forward earnings.\n\nThese metrics represent a significant departure from its five-year historical averages of 1.2x and 13.4x, respectively.\n\nThese lofty valuations imply there\u2019s less room for error should the group fail to meet earnings expectations moving forward.\n\nIts dividend yield of 4.0% also trails traditional peers such as REITs and banks.\n\nHowever, given the strong growth seen in its new business segments thus far, management\u2019s confidence in future growth, and the promise of special dividends, one could argue that these elevated valuations could be justified.\n\nGet Smart: Consider Keppel for both growth and income exposure\n\nIn conclusion, Keppel has done a decent job in transforming itself into a leaner, asset-light business with stronger profitability.\n\nThat said, current valuations are elevated, and for the stock to continue performing well, the group has to keep executing.\n\nWith its characteristics of paying solid, increasing dividends and good growth prospects, investors can consider adding Keppel to their portfolio as a \u201chybrid\u201d play.\n\nDon\u2019t let mixed signals stall your wealth building. conglomerate as both an income and growth player in the Singapore market.\n\nDividend vs Growth: Why the Trade-Off Exists\n\nThe trade-off between growth and income stocks boils down simply to a difference in priority: reinvesting for expansion (growth stocks) or income and capital stability (income stocks).\n\nA company that offers a combination of both growth and income is rare, as it requires strong and stable cash generation (to pay a steady income), alongside the availability of high-return reinvestment opportunities for growth.\n\nKeppel\u2019s Transformation: From Cyclical to Structural\n\nFirst, a short sharing on Keppel\u2019s recent transformation.\n\nKeppel has successfully shed its legacy conglomerate skin, transitioning into a lean, asset-light global manager.\n\nBy pivoting away from the highly cyclical offshore and marine sector, the group is now a specialist operator in the \u201cNew Economy\u201d trifecta: Infrastructure, Connectivity, and Real Estate.\n\nThis shift doesn\u2019t just improve margins, but it also positions Keppel at the epicentre of multi-decade tailwinds like the energy transition and the digitalisation boom.\n\nTo achieve this, the group has been divesting non-core assets, such as the recent sale of its stake in M1, to better focus on its new strategy.\n\nThe Dividend Case: Does Keppel Still Deliver Income?\n\nLet us now focus on its income potential.\n\nCurrently, Keppel offers a trailing dividend yield of almost 4%, with the group having paid a consistent annual dividend over the past five years.\n\nAt 4% represents a stunning annual growth of 38%.\n\nFurthermore, the conglomerate\u2019s dividends are backed by increasing cash flows from operations, with an estimated payout ratio of 58.2%.\n\nGiven the group\u2019s recurring fee income generation, there\u2019s a good case for continued dividend growth.\n\nThe Growth Case: Where Upside Comes From\n\nSo, where will future growth come from for Keppel?\n\nIts asset management business is an attractive growth opportunity: as funds under management increase, Keppel earns increasing, recurring fees with high margins.\n\nBy positioning itself at the intersection of renewable infrastructure and green energy, the group is capturing high-quality earnings as the energy transition accelerates.\n\nThis growth is further amplified by Keppel\u2019s aggressive asset monetisation, including the divesting of legacy non-core holdings, freeing up dry powder for higher-yielding projects.\n\nThis move fundamentally improves the group\u2019s return on equity (ROE) and margins.\n\nFinancial Snapshot\n\nKeppel\u2019s shares currently trade at roughly S$11.93, with a one-year range between S$6.12 and S$13.25.\n\nRevenue and net profit have seen stabilisation in recent years as the group\u2019s higher-margin new initiatives are offset by the ongoing divestment of its traditional business segments.\n\nAs of 2025, infrastructure makes up the bulk of Keppel\u2019s revenue at S$4.15 billion, with real estate at S$221 million and connectivity at S$953 million.\n\nKeppel\u2019s bottom-line improvement is also gaining traction, with operating margins more than doubling from 5.7% in 2022 to 12.7% in 2025.\n\nThis has allowed the group to steadily repair its balance sheet; net debt to EBITDA improved to 5.1x as of December 2025, down from 5.9x just a year prior.\n\nInvestors should note that the group\u2019s new business segments (New Keppel) have an ROE of 18.7%, comfortably above the overall ROE of 7.2%.\n\nAs the group continues to grow its New Keppel segment and divests its lower-margin non-core operations, this figure of 7.2% should continue trending higher in the future.\n\nWhat Makes Keppel a \u201cHybrid\u201d Stock Today And Key Risks\n\nKeppel\u2019s solid dividend yield and growth, with its exposure to secular growth trends such as infrastructure, digitalisation, and renewable energy, position the group as a rare \u201chybrid\u201d stock that offers income and growth.\n\nHowever, investors should monitor for risks such as execution risk: can Keppel continue growing its new businesses while successfully shedding its traditional operations?\n\nThere\u2019s also the cyclical risk involved, given the group\u2019s exposure to real estate.\n\nFinally, there\u2019s also a valuation risk to consider.\n\nValuation: Is the Hybrid Story Already Priced In?\n\nKeppel is currently priced for perfection, trading at 2.1x book and roughly 20.8x forward earnings.\n\nThese metrics represent a significant departure from its five-year historical averages of 1.2x and 13.4x, respectively.\n\nThese lofty valuations imply there\u2019s less room for error should the group fail to meet earnings expectations moving forward.\n\nIts dividend yield of 4.0% also trails traditional peers such as REITs and banks.\n\nHowever, given the strong growth seen in its new business segments thus far, management\u2019s confidence in future growth, and the promise of special dividends, one could argue that these elevated valuations could be justified.\n\nGet Smart: Consider Keppel for both growth and income exposure\n\nIn conclusion, Keppel has done a decent job in transforming itself into a leaner, asset-light business with stronger profitability.\n\nThat said, current valuations are elevated, and for the stock to continue performing well, the group has to keep executing.\n\nWith its characteristics of paying solid, increasing dividends and good growth prospects, investors can {"title": "Trump aims to seal Iran deal, says truce extension unlikely", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/trump-aims-seal-iran-deal-142809945.html", "text": "President Donald Trump said he\u2019s not likely to extend the two-week ceasefire with Iran, increasing the urgency for negotiators to conclude a deal to end the war.\n\n(April 21): President Donald Trump said he\u2019s not likely to extend the two-week ceasefire with Iran, increasing the urgency for negotiators to conclude a deal to end the war.\n\nTrump said in a Monday phone interview that the truce, which he announced April 7, expires on \u201cWednesday evening Washington time\u201d \u2014 possibly buying more time for negotiations. But the president also said it\u2019s \u201chighly unlikely that I\u2019d extend it\u201d if no deal is reached before then.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m not going to be rushed into making a bad deal. We\u2019ve got all the time in the world,\u201d the president added.\n\nIn the interview, Trump reiterated that the Strait of Hormuz would stay blockaded for now, saying \u201cthe Iranians desperately want it opened. I\u2019m not opening it until a deal is signed.\u201d Iran previously said it would open the critical waterway for energy supplies to international shipping, but reversed that decision in light of Trump\u2019s refusal to follow suit.\n\nDetails about the next negotiating session, expected to take place in Pakistan, started to come into focus on Monday. Iran is also sending a team, according to people familiar with the plans who declined to be identified, although it is not clear who would lead the delegation. Earlier, Tehran said it was hesitant to participate in further peace talks with the US.\n\nVice-President JD Vance is leaving later on Monday to resume negotiations, \u201ceither Tuesday night or Wednesday morning,\u201d Trump said. He is expected to be joined by Trump\u2019s son-in-law Jared Kushner and special envoy Steve Witkoff.\n\nThe president sounded an optimistic note about the discussions, saying he would love to participate in person, but did not think it would be necessary.\n\n\u201cThere\u2019s going to be a meeting. They want a meeting, and they should want a meeting. And it can work out well,\u201d Trump said.\n\nAt the same time, both sides sought to jockey for leverage ahead of negotiations. Iranian President Masoud Pezeshkian posted on X that \u201cdeep historical mistrust in Iran toward US gov conduct remains\u201d and declared that \u201cIranians do not submit to force.\u201d That message came after Trump warned that Iran would \u201cbe hit very hard\u201d if no deal was reached.\n\nIran\u2019s Parliament Speaker Mohammad Bagher Ghalibaf, who led the country\u2019s delegation in the first round of talks, said his government doesn\u2019t accept the premise of negotiations under the shadow of threats. \u201cBy imposing a blockade and violating the ceasefire, Donald Trump intends to turn the negotiating table into a table of surrender, or to justify renewed warmongering,\u201d he wrote in a post on X.\n\nStill, Trump\u2019s comments and Tehran\u2019s decision to dispatch negotiators represented fresh signals the two sides are continuing to work on a deal to end the war that began in late February, when the US and Israel struck Iran. Those attacks prompted Iranian forces to hit US bases in the region and destroy oil and gas infrastructure belonging to American allies in the Persian Gulf, triggering a worldwide energy crisis.\n\nEvents of the last few days have shifted rapidly, underscoring the risks if the talks are derailed.\n\nEquities dropped from all-time highs on Trump\u2019s comments about a ceasefire extension, pausing a five-day winning streak. Oil prices rose on Monday, with benchmarks up by more than 5% and Brent trading near US$95 a barrel as of 2.10pm in New York. Investors are closely watching how or when energy flows through the strait will meaningfully resume.\n\nLast Friday, Trump posted on social media that a deal was all but agreed to and Iran announced it was reopening the strait. But shortly afterward, Tehran shuttered the waterway again when Trump declined to call off the US blockade. Over the weekend, the US Navy seized an Iranian-flagged cargo ship in the Gulf of Oman.\n\n\u201cI have it closed. I took their ship. I got five other ships I\u2019ll take today if I have to,\u201d Trump said in the phone interview.\n\nBeyond the strait, arguably the most fraught issue is Iran\u2019s nuclear program. Trump has demanded Iran forswear any ambitions for a nuclear weapon and hand over stockpiles of enriched uranium. Tehran has balked at giving up its uranium and has said its nuclear program is for peaceful purposes.\n\nTrump and advisers see his varying comments about what might happen if the ceasefire deadline lapses as creating strategic ambiguity that the US could exploit in talks, said a White House official, who requested anonymity to describe internal thinking.\n\nYet that uncertainty has the potential to create misunderstandings with Iranian negotiators, who are simultaneously grappling with internal divisions among the country\u2019s leaders.\n\nConservative elements within the Iranian government and military leadership, including those at the top of the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps, have taken the continuation of the US blockade as a further signal that Trump can\u2019t be trusted, according to US and Iranian officials.\n\nThe IRGC\u2019s leader, Ahmad Vahidi, is among those in that camp and is pushing for a tough negotiating stance, people familiar with the dynamics said.\n\nThere is a divide between the likes of Vahidi and less ideological figures, such as Pezeshkian and Foreign Minister Abbas Araghchi, who are more inclined to reach an accord with Washington, said the US and Iranian officials.\n\nDespite the standoff, there\u2019s still a good chance of a deal between the US and Iran in the next few days that effectively ends the war, even if more negotiations are needed over nuclear and military issues, the officials said.\n\nTrump is facing pressure at home to end the war, with polls showing most Americans disapproving of the conflict. The president campaigned on keeping the US out of foreign entanglements and lowering consumer prices, two pledges strained by his decision to launch the war.\n\nHe has sought to assuage those worries, insisting that fuel prices will fall quickly once the war ends and that the US is not embroiled in a quagmire.\n\nThe conflict has already stretched beyond the four- to six-week timeline Trump initially set, and he has repeatedly suggested the conflict was nearing a conclusion. At the same time, he\u2019s urged Americans to have patience, noting that other US wars dragged on for years.\n\n\u201cVietnam lasted how many decades, right? Vietnam lasted years. Afghanistan lasted years. They all lasted years,\u201d Trump said. \u201cI\u2019m not going to be rushed into making a bad deal by treasonous senators and treasonous congresspeople.\u201d\n\nUploaded by Isabelle Francis\n\nSee Also:\n\nClick here to stay updated with the Latest Business & Investment News in Singapore\n\nRead more stories about where the money flows, and analysis of the biggest market stories from Singapore and around the World\n\nGet in-depth insights from our expert contributors, and dive into financial and economic trends\n\nFollow the market issue situation with our daily updates\n\nOr want more Lifestyle and Passion stories? Click here"}

{"title": "3 Dividend Stocks I\u2019d Buy As Inflation Hits", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/3-dividend-stocks-d-buy-233000803.html", "text": "Inflation rarely announces itself.\n\nIt tends to rear its ugly head through the cost of everyday items and in bills that slowly start to rise, eating into our savings and fixed income investments.\n\nAnd that\u2019s why investors turn to stocks that pay dividends during market uncertainty.\n\nHowever, not all such stocks are created equal.\n\nSome offer far more resilience over the course of time.\n\nHere are the three dividend stocks that stand out when inflation starts to take a toll on our finances.\n\nWhy Dividend Stocks Can Help During Inflation\n\nDividend investing can provide steady income and help cushion against market downturns.\n\nStrong businesses with high pricing power can raise prices and protect their margins, supporting consistent, reliable dividend payments across various market cycles.\n\nGrowing payouts serve as an effective mechanism to offset rising living costs by increasing income streams that can outpace inflation.\n\nWhat I Look for When Inflation Is Rising\n\nTop investors look for a combination of pricing power and essential demand to protect portfolios and maintain profit margins.\n\nFocusing on strong and consistent free cash flow is a reliable indicator, as it identifies companies that generate real cash, rather than just accounting profits.\n\nDividend sustainability and growth potential are the bread and butter of a robust investment strategy.\n\nThis is because companies with low debt and a track record of consistent dividend increases tend to outperform over time, as their payouts are better supported through changing market conditions.\n\nKeppel Ltd. (SGX: BN4) \u2014 The Pricing Power Leader\n\nKeppel, a leading Singapore blue-chip company, runs a tight ship as a global asset manager with a clear focus on growing its income from infrastructure, real assets, and fund management.\n\nMost of its projects rely on long-term contracts or regulated pricing, which helps keep margins steady even when costs rise.\n\nWhile revenue edged up 3.4% year on year (YoY) to S$5.98 billion in FY2025, the group delivered much stronger profit growth from its core businesses.\n\nKeppel\u2019s continuing operations lifted net profit by 39% YoY to S$1.1 billion.\n\nThis divergence between profit and revenue points to improving profitability, driven by stronger pricing discipline and higher-value income streams.\n\nKeppel also ramped up its total dividend to S$0.47 per share \u2013 38% higher than last year.\n\nAt the current share price of S$11.88, that works out to a yield of about 4%.\n\nThis highlights how pricing power and being a broad-based market leader is one of the strongest defences against inflation.\n\nOCBC Bank (SGX: O39) \u2014 The Dividend Growth Compounder\n\nOCBC\u2019s dividend growth has been both consistent and accelerating in recent years.\n\nIn the past five years, total dividends almost doubled, moving from S$0.53 to about S$0.99, driven by solid earnings and careful capital management.\n\nIgnoring special payouts, ordinary dividends still climbed from S$0.53 per share in 2021 to S$0.83 per share in 2025, a clear sign the trend is heading upward.\n\nWith its FY2025 dividend at S$0.99 per share and the current share price sitting around S$22.72, OCBC\u2019s yield stands at 4.4%.\n\nOCBC hit a big milestone on 1 April 2026, joining DBS in a rare group of Singapore companies with a market capitalisation above S$100 billion.\n\nBacked by its latest financial results for FY2025, showing net profit of S$7.42 billion and record total income of S$14.6 billion, OCBC is in a strong position to keep rewarding investors.\n\nMapletree Industrial Trust (SGX: ME8U), or MIT \u2014 The High-Quality Income Anchor\n\nMIT stands out as a steady income anchor due to its diversified portfolio \u2013 covering everything from data centres and business parks to high-tech buildings.\n\nBesides some short-term bumps, mostly from currency swings and lease renewals, its Singapore assets keep pulling their weight.\n\nOccupancies remain strong, and rents keep trending up, which helps keep investors at ease.\n\nIts latest quarterly results (3QFY2025/26) back this up. MIT delivered a distribution per unit (DPU) of S$0.0317 \u2013 a slight dip of 0.3% from the quarter before.\n\nNonetheless, distributions have stayed stable over the years, typically landing between S$0.12 and S$0.14 per unit.\n\nWith a unit price of S$2.07 and an annualised DPU of S$0.13, its yield sits at 6.3%.\n\nThat puts MIT near the top for dependable income for S-REITs.\n\nFrom a balance sheet perspective, MIT stays solid.\n\nLeverage sits at 37.2%, with an interest coverage ratio of 3.9 times as of 31 December 2025.\n\nEven as borrowing costs go up, it has kept plenty of financial wiggle room.\n\nBottom line: In choppy markets, it pays to anchor your portfolio with something you can trust.\n\nWhat I Would Avoid\n\nAvoiding high-yield stocks with weak cash flow is an essential strategy for protecting capital.\n\nThese are \u201cdividend traps\u201d, or companies with high yields driven by falling share prices, which often lead to dividend cuts.\n\nIt also pays to steer clear of companies that rely heavily on debt.\n\nIn a rising rate and inflationary environment, leverage can quickly become a burden, increasing both risk and portfolio volatility.\n\nGet Smart: Inflation Rewards the Right Kind of Income\n\nWhen inflation strikes, we need to repeat this: Not every dividend stock gives the same protection.\n\nIt\u2019s not just about how much you earn, but whether your income can keep up as prices rise.\n\nThe strongest dividend stocks are those that pair solid fundamentals with the ability to steadily grow their payouts over time.\n\nIt\u2019s not just your imagination \u2013 filling up the tank is hitting the wallet harder than it has in years. With oil prices whipsawing and the NASDAQ behaving like a roller coaster, \u201cparalysis by analysis\u201d is a real risk for investors right now. (SGX: BN4) \u2014 The Pricing Power Leader\n\nKeppel, a leading Singapore blue-chip company, runs a tight ship as a global asset manager with a clear focus on growing its income from infrastructure, real assets, and fund management.\n\nMost of its projects rely on long-term contracts or regulated pricing, which helps keep margins steady even when costs rise.\n\nWhile revenue edged up 3.4% year on year (YoY) to S$5.98 billion in FY2025, the group delivered much stronger profit growth from its core businesses.\n\nKeppel\u2019s continuing operations lifted net profit by 39% YoY to S$1.1 billion.\n\nThis divergence between profit and revenue points to improving profitability, driven by stronger pricing discipline and higher-value income streams.\n\nKeppel also ramped up its total dividend to S$0.47 per share \u2013 38% higher than last year.\n\nAt the current share price of S$11.88, that works out to a yield of about 4%.\n\nThis highlights how pricing power and being a broad-based market leader is one of the strongest defences against inflation.\n\nOCBC Bank (SGX: O39) \u2014 The Dividend Growth Compounder\n\nOCBC\u2019s dividend growth has been both consistent and accelerating in recent years.\n\nIn the past five years, total dividends almost doubled, moving from S$0.53 to about S$0.99, driven by solid earnings and careful capital management.\n\nIgnoring special payouts, ordinary dividends still climbed from S$0.53 per share in 2021 to S$0.83 per share in 2025, a clear sign the trend is heading upward.\n\nWith its FY2025 dividend at S$0.99 per share and the current share price sitting around S$22.72, OCBC\u2019s yield stands at 4.4%.\n\nOCBC hit a big milestone on 1 April 2026, joining DBS in a rare group of Singapore companies with a market their weight.\n\nOccupancies remain strong, and rents keep trending up, which helps keep investors at ease.\n\nIts latest quarterly results (3QFY2025/26) back this up. S&P 500 contracts were up slightly in early trading after the index pulled back from record highs on Monday, snapping a five-day advance amid losses in several tech giants. Apple Inc. shares declined in late trading after the company named John Ternus as its next chief.\n\nPresident Donald Trump said he is unlikely to extend the truce with Iran if no agreement is reached before its deadline, increasing the urgency for negotiators to conclude a deal to end the war. West Texas Intermediate crude for June fell as much as 2.2% to around US$86 a barrel in early trading Tuesday, after gaining 5.8% in the prior session.\n\nDetails about the next negotiating session, expected to take place in Pakistan, started to come into focus on Monday. Iran is also sending a team, according to people familiar with the plans who declined to be identified, although it is not clear who would lead the delegation. Earlier, Tehran said it was hesitant to participate in further peace talks with the US.\n\nWith the ceasefire set to expire on Wednesday evening Washington time, attention is turning to whether the US and Iran can resume negotiations to ease tensions and reopen the critical waterway, after initial talks in Islamabad failed.\n\n\u201cMarkets are once again grappling with a rapidly shifting narrative in the Middle East, as the past 48 hours have delivered both optimism and renewed concern,\u201d said Daniela Hathorn, senior market analyst at Capital.com, adding that the market feels \u201cstuck at a crossroads\u201d as a result of the jostling.\n\nTransits through Hormuz have reduced to a trickle as Iran tightens control in retaliation for strikes. On Friday, that paralysis appeared to be at an end, with Tehran saying it would reopen the waterway, before reversing course as the US maintained a naval blockade and attacked an Iranian ship.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m not going to be rushed into making a bad deal,\u201d Trump said, adding \u201cwe\u2019ve got all the time in the world.\u201d The US president noted a delegation was on its way to Pakistan even as Iran held back from saying whether it would take part in further talks.\n\nBeyond the strait, arguably the most fraught issue is Iran\u2019s nuclear program. Trump has demanded Iran forswear any ambitions for a nuclear weapon and hand over stockpiles of enriched uranium. Tehran has balked at giving up its uranium and has said its nuclear program is for peaceful purposes."}

{"title": "Trump aims to seal Iran deal, says truce extension unlikely", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/trump-aims-seal-iran-deal-142809164.html", "text": "President Donald Trump unlikely to extend the Iran ceasefire, warns against hasty deals. Vice-President JD Vance set Mon/Tues morning in Pakistan; expects Jared Kushner and Steve Witkoff to join in.\n\n(April 21) : President Donald Trump said he\u2019s not likely to extend the two-week ceasefire with Iran, increasing the urgency for negotiators to conclude a deal to end the war.\n\nTrump said in a Monday phone interview that the truce, which he announced April 7, expires on \u201cWednesday evening Washington time\u201d \u2014 possibly buying more time for negotiations. But the president also said it\u2019s \u201chighly unlikely that I\u2019d extend it\u201d if no deal is reached before then.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m not going to be rushed into making a bad deal. We\u2019ve got all the time in the world,\u201d the president added.\n\nIn the interview, Trump reiterated that the Strait of Hormuz would stay blockaded for now, saying \u201cthe Iranians desperately want it opened. I\u2019m not opening it until a deal is signed.\u201d Iran previously said it would open the critical waterway for energy supplies to international shipping, but reversed that decision in light of Trump\u2019s refusal to follow suit.\n\nDetails about the next negotiating session, expected to take place in Pakistan, started to come into focus on Monday. Iran is also sending a team, according to people familiar with the plans who declined to be identified, although it is not clear who would lead the delegation. Earlier, Tehran said it was hesitant to participate in further peace talks with the US.\n\nVice President JD Vance is leaving later on Monday to resume negotiations, \u201ceither Tuesday night or Wednesday morning,\u201d Trump said. He is expected to be joined by Trump\u2019s son-in-law Jared Kushner and special envoy Steve Witkoff.\n\nThe president sounded an optimistic note about the discussions, saying he would love to participate in person, but did not think it would be necessary.\n\n\u201cThere\u2019s going to be a meeting. They want a meeting, and they should want a meeting. And it can work out well,\u201d Trump said.\n\nAt the same time, both sides sought to jockey for leverage ahead of negotiations. Iranian President Masoud Pezeshkian posted on X that \u201cdeep historical mistrust in Iran toward U.S. gov conduct remains\u201d and declared that \u201cIranians do not submit to force.\u201d That message came after Trump warned that Iran would \u201cbe hit very hard\u201d if no deal was reached.\n\nIran\u2019s Parliament Speaker Mohammad Bagher Ghalibaf, who led the country\u2019s delegation in the first round of talks, said his government doesn\u2019t accept the premise of negotiations under the shadow of threats. \u201cBy imposing a blockade and violating the ceasefire, Donald Trump intends to turn the negotiating table into a table of surrender, or to justify renewed warmongering,\u201d he wrote in a post on X.\n\nStill, Trump\u2019s comments and Tehran\u2019s decision to dispatch negotiators represented fresh signals the two sides are continuing to work on a deal to end the war that began in late February, when the US and Israel struck Iran. Those attacks prompted Iranian forces to hit US bases in the region and destroy oil and gas infrastructure belonging to American allies in the Persian Gulf, triggering a worldwide energy crisis.\n\nEvents of the last few days have shifted rapidly, underscoring the risks if the talks are derailed.\n\nEquities dropped from all-time highs on Trump\u2019s comments about a ceasefire extension, pausing a five-day winning streak. Oil prices rose on Monday, with benchmarks up by more than 5% and Brent trading near $95 a barrel as of 2:10 p.m. in New York. Investors are closely watching how or when energy flows through the strait will meaningfully resume.\n\nLast Friday, Trump posted on social media that a deal was all but agreed to and Iran announced it was reopening the strait. But shortly afterward, Tehran shuttered the waterway again when Trump declined to call off the US blockade. Over the weekend, the US Navy seized an Iranian-flagged cargo ship in the Gulf of Oman.\n\n\u201cI have it closed. I took their ship. I got five other ships I\u2019ll take today if I have to,\u201d Trump said in the phone interview.\n\nBeyond the strait, arguably the most fraught issue is Iran\u2019s nuclear program. Trump has demanded Iran forswear any ambitions for a nuclear weapon and hand over stockpiles of enriched uranium. Tehran has balked at giving up its uranium and has said its nuclear program is for peaceful purposes.\n\nTrump and advisers see his varying comments about what might happen if the ceasefire deadline lapses as creating strategic ambiguity that the US could exploit in talks, said a White House official, who requested anonymity to describe internal thinking.\n\nYet that uncertainty has the potential to create misunderstandings with Iranian negotiators, who are simultaneously grappling with internal divisions among the country\u2019s leaders.\n\nConservative elements within the Iranian government and military leadership, including those at the top of the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps, have taken the continuation of the US blockade as a further signal that Trump can\u2019t be trusted, according to US and Iranian officials.\n\nThe IRGC\u2019s leader, Ahmad Vahidi, is among those in that camp and is pushing for a tough negotiating stance, people familiar with the dynamics said.\n\nThere is a divide between the likes of Vahidi and less ideological figures, such as Pezeshkian and Foreign Minister Abbas Araghchi, who are more inclined to reach an accord with Washington, said the US and Iranian officials.\n\nDespite the standoff, there\u2019s still a good chance of a deal between the US and Iran in the next few days that effectively ends the war, even if more negotiations are needed over nuclear and military issues, the officials said.\n\nTrump is facing pressure at home to end the war, with polls showing most Americans disapproving of the conflict. The president campaigned on keeping the US out of foreign entanglements and lowering consumer prices, two pledges strained by his decision to launch the war.\n\nHe has sought to assuage those worries, insisting that fuel prices will fall quickly once the war ends and that the US is not embroiled in a quagmire.\n\nThe conflict has already stretched beyond the four-to-six week timeline Trump initially set, and he has repeatedly suggested the conflict was nearing a conclusion. At the same time, he\u2019s urged Americans to have patience, noting that other US wars dragged on for years.\n\n\u201cVietnam lasted how many decades, right? Vietnam lasted years. Afghanistan lasted years. They all lasted years,\u201d Trump said. \u201cI\u2019m not going to be rushed into making a bad deal by treasonous senators and treasonous congresspeople.\u201d\n\nuploaded by Isabelle Francis\n\nSee Also:\n\nClick here to stay updated with the Latest Business & Investment News in Singapore\n\nRead more stories about where the money flows, and analysis of the biggest market stories from Singapore and around the World\n\nGet in-depth insights from our expert contributors, and dive into financial and economic trends\n\nFollow the market issue situation with our daily updates\n\nOr want more Lifestyle and Passion stories? Brent closed 5.6% higher at over US$95, while West Texas Intermediate dropped to about US$86.\n\n(April 21) : Oil slipped on signs that Iran will attend negotiations with the US in Islamabad before a ceasefire between the sides ends.\n\nWest Texas Intermediate for June fell as much as 2.2% to around US$86 a barrel, while Brent closed 5.6% higher on Monday at more than US$95. Iran is sending a team to the Pakistani capital, according to people familiar with the plans who declined to be identified. Earlier, Tehran had said it was hesitant to participate in further peace talks with the US.\n\nVice President JD Vance is leaving later on Monday to resume negotiations, \u201ceither Tuesday night or Wednesday morning,\u201d Donald Trump said in a phone interview on Monday. The US president said it\u2019s \u201chighly unlikely\u201d that he\u2019d extend the truce, which expires on \u201cWednesday evening Washington time.\u201d\n\nOil prices have been buffeted in recent days amid rapidly shifting perceptions of the negotiations\u2019 status and whether ships can navigate the Strait of Hormuz \u2014 the waterway through which nearly a quarter of the world\u2019s crude normally transits. The standoff over Hormuz threatens to deepen the global energy crisis and is just one of the unresolved issues between Iran and the US, which also include the Islamic Republic\u2019s nuclear capabilities and Israel\u2019s invasion of Lebanon.\n\n\u201cTraders are still trading newsworthy comments from either side and are hoping that the supply disruption will be short-lived,\u201d said Michael Tamvakis, professor of commodity economics and finance at Bayes Business School.\n\nMonday\u2019s session saw conflicting statements from Trump about the timing and viability of peace talks. Oil extended gains after he said that the US would continue to block the strait for Iran-linked ships until an agreement is finalized.\n\nMeanwhile, Hormuz flows remain at a virtual standstill. Oil prices could rise to US$110 a barrel if traffic in the waterway remains disrupted for another month, according to Citigroup.\n\nuploaded by Isabelle Francis\n\nSee Also:"}

{"title": "Amazon to invest an additional US$5 billion in Anthropic", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/amazon-invest-additional-us-5-141537848.html", "text": "Amazon's investment boosts cloud and chip capabilities for Anthropic. Deal includes US$5 billion additional investment, potentially reaching $20B over time; Amazon already invested USD8bn previously.\n\n(April 21) : Amazon.com Inc. is investing an additional US$5 billion in Anthropic PBC, and may inject US$20 billion more over time, a deal that deepens the companies\u2019 ties in an increasingly competitive artificial intelligence industry.\n\nAnthropic, which makes the Claude chatbot and coding tool, plans to spend more than US$100 billion over the next 10 years on Amazon\u2019s cloud technologies and chips, the companies said in a statement on Monday. Amazon shares gained more than 3% on the news in after-hours trading.\n\nAmazon was already one of Anthropic\u2019s biggest backers, with prior investments totaling US$8 billion. For Amazon, the partnership has given its cloud business a leading artificial intelligence model and a major customer for its home-built Trainium line of AI chips. Anthropic, meanwhile, has had access to Amazon\u2019s massive roster of corporate clients. More than 100,000 customers run Claude models on Amazon Web Services, the companies said.\n\nAnthropic PBC, founded in 2021 by several former employees of OpenAI, is widely expected to list shares in an initial public offering as soon as this year. Anthropic has been racing to persuade more businesses to pay for its software to help offset the immense cost of developing AI. The company clinched a US$30 billion funding round in February that valued the San Francisco startup at US$380 billion, and has since drawn investor offers at a valuation of over US$800 billion.\n\nThough the company has been on a winning streak this year with popular products including its Claude Code AI tool, it\u2019s also locked in a dispute with the US government over AI safeguards \u2014 a fight that has led to legal action from Anthropic and that the company has said threatens its business.\n\nAmazon says it remains a minority investor, and is not represented on the company\u2019s board or trust. The size of Amazon\u2019s investments are tied to \u201ccertain commercial milestones,\u201d Amazon said.\n\nuploaded by Isabelle Francis\n\nSee Also:"}

{"title": "Keppel REIT\u2019s NPI rises 9.7% y-o-y in 1QFY2026", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/keppel-reit-npi-rises-9-154400099.html", "text": "Share of results of joint ventures increased by 37.6% y-o-y due mainly to contribution from the additional one-third interest in Marina Bay Financial Centre Tower 3.\n\nKeppel REIT\u2019s net property income (NPI) rose 9.7% y-o-y in 1QFY2026 ended March 31 \u201cmainly to contributions from Top Ryde City Shopping Centre and increased occupancy at Ocean Financial Centre\u201d.\n\nShare of results of joint ventures increased by 37.6% y-o-y due mainly to contribution from the additional one-third interest in Marina Bay Financial Centre (MBFC) Tower 3 (announced in December 2025), along with higher rentals and lower borrowing costs.\n\nKeppel REIT\u2019s share of results from joint ventures comprises its one-third interests in One Raffles Quay and Marina Bay Financial Centre (Towers 1 and 2 and Marina Bay Link Mall), two-third interest in MBFC Tower 3 and 50% interests in 8 Chifley Square and David Malcolm Justice Centre.\n\nKeppel REIT pays distributions half-yearly. Distributable income from operations during the quarter rose 19.7% y-o-y to $57.9 million.\n\nAs at March 31, the weighted average lease expiry (WALE) for the portfolio and the top 10 tenants was at approximately 4.4 years and 8.0 years respectively.\n\nAggregate leverage was 40.2%, with a weighted average term to maturity (WATM) of 2.6 years.\n\nFor 1QFY2026, the weighted average cost of debt was 3.16% per annum. Excluding the effects of equity bridge loans obtained to preliminarily fund the acquisition of an additional one-third interest in MBFC Tower 3 that were repaid in full on Jan 20, it would be 3.27% per annum.\n\nThe interest coverage ratio was 2.6 times. As at March 31, 62% of total borrowings was on fixed rates, and sustainability-focused funding was at 79% of total borrowings.\n\nDuring the quarter, Keppel REIT committed more than 450,000 sq ft (attributable area of approximately 240,800 sq ft) of leases. New and expansion office demand was primarily driven by the banking, insurance and financial services (73.9%) sector.\n\n1QFY2026 portfolio occupancy increased to 97.1% from 96.7% in 4QFY2025 as a result of higher office occupancy and stable occupancy at Top Ryde City Shopping Centre in Sydney.\n\nRental reversion for the portfolio for 1QFY2026 was at 17.2%. The weighted average signing rent of Keppel REIT\u2019s Singapore CBD office leases was approximately $13.26 psf per month in 1QFY2026, while the average rent of leases expiring in FY2026 is $11.98 psf per month.\n\nChua Hsien Yang, CEO of the manager, says: \u201cKeppel REIT continued to record strong rental reversion of 17.2% in 1QFY2026, with the portfolio enjoying a high occupancy of 97.1%. While the macroeconomic environment and Middle East conflict present a more volatile operating environment, Keppel REIT remains anchored by our robust underlying performance and supported by favourable market fundamentals.\u201d"}
{"title": "Keppel REIT\u2019s NPI rises 9.7% y-o-y in 1QFY2026", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/keppel-reit-npi-rises-9-154400099.html", "text": "Share of results of joint ventures increased by 37.6% y-o-y due mainly to contribution from the additional one-third interest in Marina Bay Financial Centre Tower 3.\n\nKeppel REIT\u2019s net property income (NPI) rose 9.7% y-o-y in 1QFY2026 ended March 31 \u201cmainly to contributions from Top Ryde City Shopping Centre and increased occupancy at Ocean Financial Centre\u201d.\n\nShare of results of joint ventures increased by 37.6% y-o-y due mainly to contribution from the additional one-third interest in Marina Bay Financial Centre (MBFC) Tower 3 (announced in December 2025), along with higher rentals and lower borrowing costs.\n\nKeppel REIT\u2019s share of results from joint ventures comprises its one-third interests in One Raffles Quay and Marina Bay Financial Centre (Towers 1 and 2 and Marina Bay Link Mall), two-third interest in MBFC Tower 3 and 50% interests in 8 Chifley Square and David Malcolm Justice Centre.\n\nKeppel REIT pays distributions half-yearly. Distributable income from operations during the quarter rose 19.7% y-o-y to $57.9 million.\n\nAs at March 31, the weighted average lease expiry (WALE) for the portfolio and the top 10 tenants was at approximately 4.4 years and 8.0 years respectively.\n\nAggregate leverage was 40.2%, with a weighted average term to maturity (WATM) of 2.6 years.\n\nFor 1QFY2026, the weighted average cost of debt was 3.16% per annum. As at March 31, 62% of total borrowings was on fixed rates, and sustainability-focused funding was at 79% of total borrowings.\n\nDuring the quarter, Keppel REIT committed more than 450,000 sq ft (attributable area of approximately 240,800 sq ft) of leases. New and expansion office demand was primarily driven by the banking, insurance and financial services (73.9%) sector.\n\n1QFY2026 portfolio occupancy increased to 97.1% from 96.7% in 4QFY2025 as a result of higher office occupancy and stable occupancy at Top Ryde City Shopping Centre in Sydney.\n\nRental reversion for the portfolio for 1QFY2026 was at 17.2%. The weighted average signing rent of Keppel REIT\u2019s Singapore CBD office leases was approximately $13.26 psf per month in 1QFY2026, while the average rent of leases expiring in FY2026 is $11.98 psf per month.\n\nChua Hsien Yang, CEO of the manager, says: \u201cKeppel REIT continued to record strong rental reversion of 17.2% in 1QFY2026, with the portfolio enjoying a high occupancy of 97.1%. While the macroeconomic environment and Middle East conflict present a more volatile operating environment, Keppel REIT remains anchored by our robust underlying performance and supported by favourable market fundamentals.\u201d"}
{"title": "California man allegedly swapped LEGO bricks for dry pasta, returned 70 boxes to Target for $34K in refunds", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/california-man-allegedly-swapped-lego-203000314.html", "text": "Jarrelle Augustine's alleged scheme was almost elegant. Buy a $400 LEGO Star Wars set. Pour the bricks out at home. Refill the box with dry pasta, which rattles just enough to fool a return clerk. Reseal it. Bring it back for a full refund.\n\nIrvine police say the 28-year-old Paramount, California, resident ran that playbook roughly 70 times at Target stores in California, Texas, Tennessee, New Jersey and Florida, netting about $34,000 in fraudulent refunds before officers tracked him to a Los Angeles County apartment on April 15 and found the unboxed bricks stockpiled inside (1).\n\nInvestigators said the dried \"durum wheat semolina\" pasta Augustine used mimicked the weight and sound of LEGO bricks shifting inside a sealed box.\n\nThe targets weren't random. \"These were Star Wars sets and Marvel sets, which have a very high value on the secondary market,\" Officer Ziggy Azarcon told CBS News (2).\n\nMust Read\n\nThanks to Jeff Bezos, you can now become a landlord for as little as $100 \u2014 and no, you don't have to deal with tenants or fix freezers. Here's how\n\nRobert Kiyosaki says this 1 asset will surge 400% in a year and begs investors not to miss this \u2018explosion\u2019\n\nDave Ramsey warns nearly 50% of Americans are making 1 big Social Security mistake \u2014 here\u2019s how to fix it ASAP\n\nA LEGO crime wave continues\n\nJust a week before Augustine's arrest, on April 8, Kern County deputies recovered roughly $1 million worth of stolen LEGO sets after spotting two Amazon-branded box trucks fleeing a scene in Mojave (3). Investigators later located two abandoned freight trailers that had been stolen while transporting goods from Fort Worth, Texas, to Moreno Valley, California. Three Southern California men were booked on cargo theft, possession of a stolen vehicle and conspiracy charges.\n\nSix months earlier, Santa Rosa police served a warrant at a Lake County home and walked into what looked like a LEGO crime scene: tens of thousands of loose pieces scattered across desks, hundreds of minifigures beheaded and sorted by facial expression, unopened sets stacked along the hallway walls (4). The total seized LEGO was valued at just over $6,000, but detectives described the setup as a \"systematic\" fencing operation. Robert Lopez, 39, was charged with organized retail theft after allegedly directing others to steal sets from Walmart and Target, then buying the stolen goods at a discount to flip online.\n\nIn Charlotte, North Carolina, the fallout ran longer. Former Wells Fargo banker Ryan Cahill was sentenced in November 2025 to a minimum of six years in prison for fencing more than $100,000 worth of LEGO toys stolen from area Walmart and Target stores (5). Federal filings had earlier alleged Cahill moved roughly $225,000 through an eBay account called \"brikbybrik\" (6).\n\nRetailers are adapting. Walmart has locked LEGO sets behind anti-theft glass cases in some U.S. stores, forcing customers to flag down staff to buy.\n\nWhy LEGO?\n\nSets are small, light, universally recognized and carry no serial numbers. Police have publicly flagged the \"untraceable nature\" of the product as a reason it keeps surfacing in organized retail crime cases. The secondary market \u2014 eBay, Facebook Marketplace, BrickLink \u2014 makes fencing nearly frictionless.\n\nRetail prices have climbed to the point where the math genuinely favors thieves. The Ultimate Collector Series Millennium Falcon retails at $849.99 on the LEGO shop (7). Retired sets appreciate like collectibles: a 2007 Caf\u00e9 Corner set with an original sticker price of $139.99 now trades for roughly $2,500 on the secondary market, according to tracker Brickset (8).\n\nRead More: This $1B private real estate fund is now accessible to non-millionaires. Start investing with just $10\n\nThat isn't just anecdotal. A 2022 study by economists at Moscow's Higher School of Economics, published in Research in International Business and Finance, analyzed secondary-market prices for 2,322 LEGO sets released between 1987 and 2015 and found retired sets generated an average annual return of 11%, outperforming gold, large-cap stocks and corporate bonds over the same period (9). Some sets delivered 600% to 700% returns; others lost value. The paper's title captured the pitch: \"LEGO \u2014 The Toy of Smart Investors.\"\n\nLEGO has leaned into this dynamic. The company launched its 18+ product line in 2020, since rebranded as LEGO Icons, and reported record 2024 revenue of 74.3 billion Danish kroner ($10.8 billion), up 13% year over year, with operating profit of 18.7 billion DKK (10). It's a privately held Danish company owned by the Kirk Kristiansen family through holding firm Kirkbi, which controls 75% of the group.\n\nThe bigger picture\n\nCargo theft nationwide reached an estimated $725 million in losses in 2025, a 60% jump from 2024, according to Verisk CargoNet's annual analysis (11). The average value per theft climbed 36% to $273,990. Criminal groups have grown more selective, chasing high-value shipments rather than opportunistic grabs \u2014 which is exactly the pattern the Kern County bust fits. Notably, Kern County itself saw an 82% year-over-year jump in cargo theft incidents in 2025 per CargoNet, the largest increase of any California county.\n\nCalifornia's Organized Retail Crime Task Force seized more than 272,000 stolen items in 2025 alone through 734 investigations, Gov. Gavin Newsom's office announced in January. That's up from just 24 investigations in 2019, a 31-fold jump in state-level ORC casework over six years (12). Separately, state-funded local operations between October 2023 and June 2025 recovered more than $190 million in stolen goods and arrested over 25,675 suspects (13).\n\nFor consumers, the LEGO boom cuts two ways. Retired sets can be genuine alternative assets \u2014 but buying on the secondary market means navigating an inventory where a portion is stolen. Authentication, provenance and suspiciously steep discounts are worth a harder look. For someone like Augustine, cashing in apparently required only a grocery item and a straight face.\n\nYou May Also Like\n\nTaxes are going to change for retirees under Trump\u2019s \u2018big beautiful bill\u2019 \u2014 here are 4 reasons you can\u2019t afford to waste time\n\nRobert Kiyosaki issues grim warning for baby boomers: many could be \u2018wiped out\u2019 and homeless \u2018all over\u2019 the country\n\nVanguard\u2019s outlook on U.S. stocks is raising alarm bells for retirees. Here\u2019s why and how to protect yourself\n\nMillionaires under 43 are reshaping investing \u2014 just 25% of their portfolios are in stocks. Here\u2019s where their money is going\n\nJoin 250,000+ readers and get Moneywise\u2019s best stories and exclusive interviews first \u2014 clear insights curated and delivered weekly. {"title": "Forget Florida's sunny skies and lower taxes: Why snowbirds are reversing course and retiring to New York City", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/forget-floridas-sunny-skies-lower-113500815.html", "text": "For decades, there's been a stereotypical playbook for many adults: build a career and wealth in a big city, then retire to a warm southern beach town with low taxes. The move from New York City to Florida is perhaps the most typical example.\n\nBut a recent New York Times report highlights a surprising trend: some older Americans are actually moving the other way. The numbers back it up (1).\n\nMust Read\n\nThanks to Jeff Bezos, you can now become a landlord for as little as $100 \u2014 and no, you don't have to deal with tenants or fix freezers. {"title": "Another airline shuts down for summer, cancels all flights", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/another-airline-shuts-down-summer-150734264.html", "text": "With any attempts at peace talks over Iran now fallen through multiple times, the war has created a major crisis for airlines when it comes to the cost of jet fuel and the safety of certain routes.\n\nLocal airlines such as Emirates and Etihad have been running some flights into and out of Dubai. Yet major international carriers have canceled all service into the United Arab Emirates and several nearby countries as the ripple effects of the war set off by the U.S.-Israeli strike last February continue across the Middle Eastern region.\n\nDelta Air Lines, United Airlines, Air Canada, British Airways, Air France, and KLM are among the major airlines currently not flying into Dubai due to ongoing security concerns.\n\nBeOnd flights to Maldives canceled until October 2026\n\nEstablished in 2022 as an airline with an Airbus A319 configured with all-business-class seats, Mal\u00e9-based BeOnd had lofty plans of growing into the main airline for travelers headed to the Maldives.\n\nThe airline had been running flights to the capital of the nation in the Indian Ocean associated with extreme luxury from the UAE, Saudi Arabia, and Egypt, as well as European cities such as Milan and Z\u00fcrich.\n\nPrior to the current situation, BeOnd was also preparing to launch flights from London Heathrow and Paris by December 2026, while also eying the first direct service to the Maldives from the U.S. at some point after.\n\nBut as is now apparent from the airline's booking availability and Cirium flight data, BeOnd has canceled all of its service for the summer.\n\nAlthough the airline had initially canceled only longer routes that made a stopover in Dubai as the nearest major hub, falling traveler numbers to the entire region likely led to a full grounding of the fleet in the hopes of restarting in October 2026.\n\nBeOnd promises \"flexible rebooking options\" or full refund\n\n\"If you're booked to travel with us this summer, our guest experience team will be in touch within the next 72 hours with flexible rebooking options including fee-free moves to winter, future travel within 12 months, or a full refund,\" the airline wrote in a Facebook post on April 18.\n\nThe last flight from Z\u00fcrich to Velana International (MLE) in Mal\u00e9 is scheduled to run on May 1.\n\nMore Travel News:\n\nAirline to launch unusual new flight to Cayman Islands from the U.S.\n\nWhat you can expect at Disneyland's new 'World of Frozen'\n\nUnexpected country is most luxurious travel destination for 2026\n\nU.S. government issues strange warning on Ireland travel\n\nThe airline's booking platform and Cirium flight data currently show staggered resumptions in service from cities such as Dubai, Milan, Z\u00fcrich, London, Paris, and Moscow."}

{"title": "GLP-1 boom nudges cannabis dispensaries to rethink offerings", "link": "https://finance.yahoo.com/sectors/healthcare/articles/glp-1-boom-nudges-cannabis-163755897.html", "text": "By Mrinalika Roy and Sriparna Roy\n\nApril 20 (Reuters) - The surging popularity of GLP-1 weight-loss drugs is quietly reshaping the $40 billion U.S. cannabis market, experts and industry executives said, as retailers \u200cadjust product offerings to suit changing consumer behavior tied to the therapies.\n\nUsers on online forums \u200creported diminished cravings and uncertainty about how GLP-1 therapies might influence marijuana's aftereffects - particularly appetite-driven \"munchies\" - while dispensaries noted shifting customer preferences.\n\nAlthough \u200bthe scientific data is limited, cannabis retailers are already adapting to the shift.\n\nStoops NYC, a dispensary in New York's Flatiron district, said it increasingly recommends lower-dose edibles, vapes or tinctures to customers on GLP-1 medications.\n\nOne area of immediate interaction is digestion, as GLP-1 therapies slow gastric emptying, potentially delaying the onset of edible cannabis' \u200ceffects and increasing the risk of \u2060users consuming additional doses too soon, leading to stronger-than-expected \"highs\".\n\n\"As (GLP) adoption accelerates, we are exploring ways to provide clearer guidance at the point of sale,\" said Wendy Bronfein, \u2060co-founder and chief brand officer at Curio Wellness.\n\nResearchers are beginning to test the link more directly now. The National Institute on Drug Abuse is sponsoring a clinical trial this year evaluating tirzepatide, the active ingredient in Eli \u200bLilly's weight-loss \u200bdrugs, as a potential treatment for cannabis use disorder.\n\nThe \u200bagency's director, Dr. Nora Volkow, also said \u200cretrospective analyses of electronic health records showed patients with diabetes who were prescribed GLP-1 drugs such as semaglutide had significantly better health outcomes related to cannabis use disorder, compared with those on other diabetes treatments.\n\nAnother trial by Brigham and Women's Hospital is expected to start later this year.\n\nConsumer behaviour may be shifting in other ways as well. Some users appear to be substituting cannabis for alcohol, while others are \u200cshifting to its targeted or intentional use for sleep or \u200bstress, said Steph Woods, vice president of sales at S\u014dRSE \u200bTechnology.\n\nData from cannabis education nonprofit Realm of \u200bCaring shows growing curiosity among consumers about the link between cannabis and metabolism. \u200cSince 2024, the top 20 queries on its \u200bcannabis hotline have included \u200bitems such as \"THC for weight loss\", \"weed strains that suppress appetite\", and \"edibles that don't make you hungry\"."}

{"title": "The Pentagon wants GM, Ford to build weapons and bombs \u2014 here\u2019s what happened last time during World War II", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/pentagon-wants-gm-ford-build-110500812.html", "text": "The U.S. Department of Defense is asking American automakers and other manufacturers to help build military equipment as wars in Ukraine and the Middle East deplete supplies.\n\nAccording to The Wall Street Journal (1), senior Pentagon officials have approached various companies, including General Motors (NYSE: GM), Ford (NYSE: F), GE Aerospace, and Oshkosh (NYSE: OSK), about playing a larger role in weapons production.\n\nMust Read\n\nThanks to Jeff Bezos, you can now become a landlord for as little as $100 \u2014 and no, you don't have to deal with tenants or fix freezers. Here's how\n\nRobert Kiyosaki says this 1 asset will surge 400% in a year and begs investors not to miss this \u2018explosion\u2019\n\nDave Ramsey warns nearly 50% of Americans are making 1 big Social Security mistake \u2014 here\u2019s how to fix it ASAP\n\nThese preliminary talks come amid concerns about equipment shortages and as the Trump administration pushes to put the U.S. on what Defense Secretary Pete Hegseth calls a \"wartime footing,\" backed by a proposed $1.5 trillion defense budget.\n\nDefense officials framed the request as a national security priority, asking whether companies could quickly repurpose factories and workers if needed. The Defense Department \"is committed to rapidly expanding the defense industrial base by leveraging all available commercial solutions and technologies to ensure our warfighters maintain a decisive advantage,\" a Pentagon official said (2).\n\nThis isn't the first time the Trump administration has called on American automakers, in particular. During the early days of the pandemic, they were asked to help produce ventilators and face masks (3).\n\nIt also isn't the first time the Pentagon has asked non-defense companies to build weapons, with its latest move drawing comparisons to World War II, when U.S. manufacturers rapidly converted factories to support the war effort.\n\nThe \"Arsenal of Democracy\"\n\nWhen the U.S. entered World War II after the Pearl Harbor attack in 1941, the federal government faced an urgent challenge: how to rapidly scale up production for a global war.\n\nThe solution was a sweeping mobilization of private industry, led in large part by automakers. Companies like General Motors and Ford stopped making cars for the public and retooled factories for military output, forming part of what President Franklin D. Roosevelt called the \"Arsenal of Democracy\" (4).\n\nThe results were staggering. According to the National WWII Museum (5), American manufacturers produced billions of dollars' worth of supplies, including 96,000 bombers, 86,000 tanks, 2.4 million trucks and 6.5 million rifles.\n\nFord's Willow Run plant alone built more than 8,865 B-24 bombers, with monthly output increasing from just one plane in October 1942 to anywhere up to 650 by the end of 1944 (6). General Motors, meanwhile, became the top military contractor in the U.S., delivering over $12.3 billion (7) in goods, including trucks, aircraft engines, tanks, cannons, torpedoes and machine guns (8).\n\nRead More: This $1B private real estate fund is now accessible to non-millionaires. Start investing with just $10\n\nThen vs. now\n\nToday, a small group of companies (Lockheed Martin, RTX Corporation, Boeing, Northrop Grumman and General Dynamics) dominate military production (9). Contracts also go to other firms, including the likes of General Motors, General Electric and Oshkosh Corporation, but their defense expertise is narrow and represents a small slice of their overall business (10).\n\nThis concentration of major suppliers has raised concerns, especially after the U.S. and its NATO allies began sending large quantities of weapons to Ukraine following its invasion by Russia. Shortfalls in key areas have subsequently been reported, prompting the government to even accuse the five big defense contractors of slacking on production and failing to keep up with demand (11).\n\nExpanding the defense industrial base beyond traditional contractors could reduce bottlenecks, accelerate production during crises and potentially improve quality and pricing by increasing competition.\n\nBut there are also lots of question marks. A key one is feasibility. Getting a helping hand from manufacturers of other goods is more complex than it was in the 1940s. Today's military equipment relies on complex supply chains, advanced electronics and globally sourced components, making rapid conversion far more difficult (12).\n\nOther uncertainties include whether these companies can match the quality of specialist contractors, how costly it will be to pivot production, what incentives may be needed to get them on board and whether the shift could create shortages and price increases in the other goods they make.\n\nYou May Also Like\n\nTaxes are going to change for retirees under Trump\u2019s \u2018big beautiful bill\u2019 \u2014 here are 4 reasons you can\u2019t afford to waste time\n\nRobert Kiyosaki issues grim warning for baby boomers: many could be \u2018wiped out\u2019 and homeless \u2018all over\u2019 the country\n\nVanguard\u2019s outlook on U.S. stocks is raising alarm bells for retirees. {"title": "Are You a Rich Household? Here's The Income It Takes To Be Poor, Middle Class, Or Wealthy", "link": "https://finance.yahoo.com/economy/articles/rich-household-heres-income-takes-154617254.html", "text": "Benzinga and Yahoo Finance LLC may earn commission or revenue on some items through the links below.\n\nA quick glance at a paycheck or tax return can spark the question \u2014 does this count as wealthy, or just getting by? The answer depends less on gut feeling and more on where that number lands compared to the rest of the country.\n\nThe U.S. Census Bureau reported a median household income of $83,730 in 2024, the most recent full-year benchmark. That figure serves as the baseline for defining where a household falls across income tiers.\n\nWhere Lower Income Starts\n\nLower-income status is anchored by a few key benchmarks.\n\nThe Department of Health and Human Services set the 2026 Federal Poverty Guideline at $21,640 for a two-person household. Near-poor status often extends to about $32,460.\n\nDon't Miss:\n\nThe AI Marketing Platform Backed by Insiders from Google, Meta, and Amazon \u2014 Invest at $0.91/Share\n\nYou Saved for Retirement \u2014 But Do You Know What You'll Keep After Taxes?\n\nBroader income comparisons place lower-income households at roughly $56,600 or less for a typical three-person household. That's where earnings fall well below the national midpoint.\n\nWhat Counts As Middle Class\n\nMost households fall into the middle, but the range is wider than expected.\n\nThe Pew Research Center defines middle-income households as earning between two-thirds and double the median. That puts the range for a three-person household at roughly $56,600 to $169,800.\n\nA February analysis from SmartAsset found the lower end can dip below $40,000 in some regions and climb toward $70,000 in others, while upper bounds often exceed $200,000 in higher-cost states.\n\nThe American Enterprise Institute places the core middle class between about $67,000 and $133,000, with upper-middle income stretching to around $400,000.\n\nTrending: See What AI Could Build for Your Portfolio \u2014 Try a Custom Index Now\n\nWhat It Takes To Be Considered Wealthy\n\nWealthy status begins where the middle range ends.\n\nUsing the national median from the Census Bureau as a guide, upper-class income starts above roughly $170,000.\n\nAround $170,000 to $190,000 places a household in the top 20%\n\nAround $230,000 to $250,000 reaches the top 10%\n\nAbove $650,000 to $700,000 enters the top 1%\n\nWhy It May Not Feel That Way\n\nEven if income lands in a higher bracket, it may not feel like it.\n\nThese figures reflect pre-tax income and don't account for cost of living, taxes, debt, or savings. A six-figure salary can stretch differently depending on location and financial obligations.\n\nIncome also doesn't equal wealth. Assets, investments, and long-term financial stability shape how secure a household actually is.\n\nWhere You Go From Here Matters More Than The Label\n\nThe numbers give a snapshot, but they don't define the outcome.\n\nLanding near the median places a household squarely in the middle, while moving past roughly $170,000 pushes into higher-income territory. That's the math. What matters more is what happens next.\n\nSee Also: Why Traders Are Flocking to Leveraged ETFs \u2014 And What It Means for You\n\nIncome can be increased, but it often takes time, strategy, and patience. What's more immediate is how that money is managed. Saving consistently, investing with intention, and avoiding lifestyle creep can quietly move the needle faster than a raise alone.\n\nA higher income helps, no question. But it's not the full story. The real advantage comes from what is kept, grown, and put to work over time.\n\nSo wherever the number lands today, it's less about the label and more about the direction.\n\nSo wherever your income falls, the next step often comes down to how that money is managed over time\u2014from saving and investing to planning for taxes and long-term goals.\n\nFor those looking to take a more structured approach, tools like SmartAsset connect users with vetted financial advisors who can help build personalized financial plans based on income, location, and individual financial priorities.\n\nRead Next: This 2-Minute Tool Matches Investors With Financial Advisors Based on Their Goals\n\nBuilding Wealth Across More Than Just the Market\n\nBuilding a resilient portfolio means thinking beyond a single asset or market trend. Economic cycles shift, sectors rise and fall, and no one investment performs well in every environment. That's why many investors look to diversify with platforms that provide access to real estate, fixed-income opportunities, professional financial guidance, precious metals, and even self-directed retirement accounts. By spreading exposure across multiple asset classes, it becomes easier to manage risk, capture steady returns, and create long-term wealth that isn't tied to the fortunes of just one company or industry.\n\nRad AI\n\nRAD Intel is an AI-driven marketing platform helping brands improve campaign performance by turning complex data into actionable insights for content, influencer strategy, and ROI optimization. Positioned within the multi-hundred-billion-dollar digital marketing industry, the company works with global brands across sectors to improve targeting precision and creative performance using its analytics and AI tools. With strong revenue growth, expanding enterprise contracts, and a Nasdaq ticker reserved under $RADI, RAD Intel is opening access to its Regulation A+ offering, giving investors exposure to the growing intersection of AI, marketing, and creator economy infrastructure.\n\nMode Mobile\n\nMode Mobile is changing the way people interact with their phones by letting users earn money from the same apps and activities they already use every day. Instead of platforms keeping all the advertising revenue, Mode Mobile shares a portion back with users who engage with content, play games, and scroll on their devices. Named one of Deloitte's fastest-growing software companies in North America, the company has built a large beta user base and is scaling a model that turns everyday smartphone usage into a potential income stream. For investors, Mode Mobile offers exposure to the expanding mobile advertising and attention economy through a pre-IPO opportunity tied to a new approach to user monetization.\n\nrHealth\n\nrHealth is building a space-tested diagnostics platform designed to bring lab-quality blood testing closer to patients in minutes rather than weeks. Originally validated in collaboration with NASA for use aboard the International Space Station, the technology is now being adapted for at-home and point-of-care settings to address widespread delays in diagnostic access.\n\nBacked by institutions including NASA and the NIH, rHealth is targeting the large global diagnostics market with a multi-test platform and a model built around devices, consumables, and software. With FDA registration in progress, the company is positioning itself as a potential shift toward faster, more decentralized healthcare testing.\n\nDirexion\n\nDirexion specializes in leveraged and inverse ETFs designed to help active traders express short-term market views during periods of volatility and major market events. Rather than long-term investing, these products are built for tactical use\u2014allowing investors to take magnified bullish or bearish positions across indices, sectors, and single stocks. For experienced traders, Direxion offers a way to respond quickly to changing market conditions and act on high-conviction views with greater flexibility.\n\nArrived\n\nBacked by Jeff Bezos, Arrived Homes makes real estate investing accessible with a low barrier to entry. Investors can buy fractional shares of single-family rentals and vacation homes starting with as little as $100. This allows everyday investors to diversify into real estate, collect rental income, and build long-term wealth without needing to manage properties directly.\n\nMasterworks\n\nMasterworks enables investors to diversify into blue-chip art, an alternative asset class with historically low correlation to stocks and bonds. Through fractional ownership of museum-quality works by artists like Banksy, Basquiat, and Picasso, investors gain access without the high costs or complexities of owning art outright. With hundreds of offerings and strong historical exits on select works, Masterworks adds a scarce, globally traded asset to portfolios seeking long-term diversification.\n\nFinance Advisors\n\nFinance Advisors helps Americans approach retirement with greater clarity by connecting them to vetted, fiduciary financial advisors who specialize in tax-aware retirement planning. Rather than focusing on products or investment performance alone, the platform emphasizes strategies that account for after-tax income, withdrawal sequencing, and long-term tax efficiency\u2014factors that can materially impact retirement outcomes. Free to use, Finance Advisors gives individuals with meaningful savings access to a level of planning sophistication historically reserved for high-net-worth households, helping reduce hidden tax risk and improve long-term financial confidence.\n\nBam Capital\n\nBAM Capital offers accredited investors a way to diversify beyond public markets through institutional-grade multifamily real estate. With over $1.85 billion in completed transactions and guidance from Senior Economic Advisor Tony Landa, the firm targets income and long-term growth as supply tightens and renter demand remains strong\u2014especially in Midwest markets. Its income-focused and growth-oriented funds provide exposure to real assets designed to be less tied to stock market volatility.\n\nPublic\n\nPublic is a multi-asset investing platform built for long-term investors who want more control, transparency, and innovation in how they grow wealth. Founded in 2019 as the first broker-dealer to offer commission-free, real-time fractional investing, Public now lets users invest in stocks, bonds, options, crypto, and more\u2014all in one place. Its latest feature, Generated Assets, uses AI to turn a single idea into a fully customized, investable index that can be explained and backtested before committing capital. Combined with AI-powered research tools, clear explanations of market moves, and an uncapped 1% match for transferring an existing portfolio, Public positions itself as a modern platform designed to help serious investors make more informed decisions with context.\n\nAdviserMatch\n\nAdviserMatch is a free online tool that helps individuals connect with financial advisors based on their goals, financial situation, and investment needs. Instead of spending hours researching advisors on your own, the platform asks a few quick questions and matches you with professionals who can assist with areas like retirement planning, investment strategy, and overall financial guidance. Consultations are no-obligation, and services vary by advisor, giving investors a chance to explore whether professional advice could help improve their long-term financial plan.\n\nEnergyX\n\nEnergyX is a lithium extraction company focused on making production faster and more efficient with its LiTAS\u00ae technology, which can recover over 90% of lithium in just days instead of months. Backed by General Motors and a $5 million U.S. Department of Energy grant, the company controls extensive lithium acreage in Chile and the U.S. and is working to scale one of the largest lithium production facilities. Its goal is to help meet the rapidly growing global demand for lithium, a key resource for electric vehicles, consumer electronics, and large-scale energy storage.\n\nImage: Shutterstock"}
