{"title": "Markets shudder as Strait of Hormuz starts resembling a combat zone. \u2018We\u2019re prepared to subject you to disabling fire\u2019", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/markets-shudder-strait-hormuz-starts-231324915.html", "text": "Stock futures tumbled and oil prices jumped on Sunday after hopes that the Strait of Hormuz would fully reopen were deflated over the weekend by renewed gunfire.\n\nFutures tied to the Dow Jones industrial average fell 407 points, or 0.82%. S&P 500 futures were down 0.67%, and Nasdaq futures lost 0.57%.\n\nU.S. oil futures jumped 7.14% to $89.94 a barrel, and Brent crude climbed 5.9% to $95.71. Gold fell 1.6% to $4,801.40 per ounce.\n\nThe U.S. dollar was up 0.2% against the euro and rose 0.25% against the yen. The yield on the 10-year Treasury was flat at 4.248%.\n\nOn Friday, President Donald Trump and Iran\u2019s foreign minister announced that ship traffic in the narrow waterway was completely free, sinking oil prices and triggering a massive stock rally that sent the S&P 500 to fresh highs.\n\nBut Trump also said the U.S. naval blockade on Iran would remain in place until a deal is finalized, and the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps said it still controls the strait.\n\nBy Saturday, the IRGC declared that Hormuz was closed again to all vessels, regardless of type or national origin. Ships also reported coming under attack from projectiles and small boats, likely Iran\u2019s \u201cmosquito fleet.\u201d\n\nTensions in the Persian Gulf escalated further on Sunday, when the U.S. Navy seized a ship for the first time as part of its blockade, with a destroyer firing at a vessel attempting to evade the dragnet.\n\nA statement from U.S. Central Command said the guided-missile destroyer U.S.S. Spruance intercepted the Iranian-flagged M/V Touska as it transited the north Arabian Sea en route to Bandar Abbas on the Iranian coast, sending multiple warnings that it was violating the blockade.\n\nBut after the Touska didn\u2019t comply over a six-hour period, the Spruance ordered the vessel to evacuate its engine room and fired several rounds from the destroyer\u2019s five-inch gun, disabling the propulsion system, the statement said.\n\n\u201cMotor vessel Touska, motor vessel Touska\u2014vacate your engine room, vacate your engine room,\u201d sailors aboard the Spruance said, according to a video clip released by Central Command. \u201cWe\u2019re prepared to subject you to disabling fire.\u201d\n\nOn social media, Trump said the Navy \u201cstopped them right in their tracks by blowing a hole in the engineroom,\u201d adding that the Touska was under U.S. Treasury sanctions because of its prior history of illegal activity.\n\nCentral Command added that Marines from the 31st Marine Expeditionary Unit later boarded the Touska, which remains in U.S. custody."}

Warsh holds a degree in public policy from Stanford, as well as a law degree from Harvard. He is a known figure to Trump, who interviewed him for the Fed chair post eight years ago before selecting Powell \u2014 a choice Trump regretted almost instantly.\n\nWarsh has been highly critical of the Fed in recent months, writing in an op-ed in the Wall Street Journal last year that the Fed should \u201cdiscard its forecast of stagflation\u201d and arguing that it is overlooking that AI will be a \u201csignificant\u201d force that will boost productivity and push down inflation.\n\n\u201cHe thinks you have to lower interest rates,\u201d Trump said of Warsh recently, citing the president's key litmus test for the role."}
{"title": "Everything we know about Apple's new CEO John Ternus", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/everything-we-know-about-apples-new-ceo-john-ternus-000314167.html", "text": "Apple\u2019s (AAPL) Tim Cook is stepping down from his role as CEO, turning the reins of the $4 trillion company over to senior vice president (SVP) of hardware engineering John Ternus.\n\nRumors have been swirling since at least 2024 that Ternus was up for the chief executive position, and that will become reality on Sept. 1.\n\nWhile Ternus holds one of the larger leadership roles at Apple and makes appearances at the company\u2019s high-profile product launches, including the debut of the MacBook Neo last month, he\u2019s still a relative unknown for those who haven\u2019t been following the company closely in recent years.\n\nTernus joined Apple in 2001 as a member of the company\u2019s product design team, before being elevated to VP of hardware engineering in 2013. He was named SVP of hardware engineering in 2021.\n\nThe future CEO graduated from the University of Pennsylvania with a degree in mechanical engineering and worked at Virtual Research Systems before moving to Apple.\n\nHe\u2019s the kind of perfectionist Apple is known for.\n\nDuring his keynote address at The University of Pennsylvania\u2019s Engineering Commencement in 2024, Ternus recounted arguing with a supplier over the number of grooves in the heads of screws that would sit in the back of his first Apple product, the Apple Cinema Display. The screws the supplier offered had 35 grooves, but Ternus demanded they stick to the 25 grooves Apple wanted.\n\n\u201cI distinctly remember stepping back for a minute and thinking to myself, \u2018What the hell am I doing? Is this normal?\u2019 And I thought about it, and I realized it might not be normal, but it's right,\u201d he said.\n\n\u201cIt's right because I'd already spent months working on that product, and if you're going to spend that much time on something, you should put in your very best effort. Maybe a customer notices, maybe they don't. But either way, whenever I saw one of those displays on someone's desk, it mattered to me to know that my teammates and I had considered everything about it.\u201d\n\nIn announcing the future leadership transition, Apple credited Ternus with a variety of recent successes, including helping to make the Mac lineup the most popular it's ever been, introducing the iPhone 17 lineup, and improving the AirPods.\n\nTernus, Apple said, also helped drive Apple\u2019s push to create a recycled aluminum compound that the company uses across a number of products and worked on the 3D-printed titanium in the Apple Watch Ultra 3.\n\nIn his new role, however, he\u2019ll be heading up the company during a time of major upheaval in the tech industry driven by artificial intelligence."}
{"title": "Everything we know about Apple's new CEO John Ternus", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/everything-we-know-about-apples-new-ceo-john-ternus-000314167.html", "text": "Apple\u2019s (AAPL) Tim Cook is stepping down from his role as CEO, turning the reins of the $4 trillion company over to senior vice president (SVP) of hardware engineering John Ternus.\n\nRumors have been swirling since at least 2024 that Ternus was up for the chief executive position, and that will become reality on Sept. 1.\n\nWhile Ternus holds one of the larger leadership roles at Apple and makes appearances at the company\u2019s high-profile product launches, including the debut of the MacBook Neo last month, he\u2019s still a relative unknown for those who haven\u2019t been following the company closely in recent years.\n\nTernus joined Apple in 2001 as a member of the company\u2019s product design team, before being elevated to VP of hardware engineering in 2013. {"title": "Apple CEO Tim Cook steps down: 7 big challenges for new CEO John Ternus", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/apple-ceo-tim-cook-steps-down-7-big-challenges-for-new-ceo-john-ternus-233730971.html", "text": "There's a changing of the guard at Apple (AAPL).\n\nApple said today that longtime CEO Tim Cook will step down as CEO later this year and transition to executive chairman of the board. As many on the Street expected, he will be succeeded by John Ternus, currently Apple's senior vice president of hardware engineering. Ternus will take the helm on Sept. 1.\n\n\"Investors will view this as mixed, as this was a sudden move to executive chairman [and] there was clearly a push for change at the C-suite. These will be big shoes to fill, and the timing of Cook exiting stage left as CEO could make sense but also creates questions,\" Wedbush tech analyst Dan Ives said in a note.\n\n\"Apple is making a major transition on its AI strategy, and longtime CEO and legendary Cook leaving now is a surprise. There was growing pressure on Apple to develop a successful AI strategy, and Cook must feel that the pieces are now in place heading into WWDC to hand over the reins at this time. Cook leaves a lasting legacy in Cupertino, and there will be a lot of pressure on Ternus to produce success out of the gates, especially on the AI front.\"\n\nHere are seven early to-do's for Ternus as Apple CEO. Notching early wins could go a long way in Ternus building Street cred and silencing any doubt he is the right person at the right time to lead the tech giant.\n\n1. Make Apple AI relevant.\n\nTernus will get a head start on this from Cook, but he needs to build on it and be unafraid to ink other partnerships. Apple and Google (GOOG) recently entered a multiyear partnership to integrate a custom version of the Gemini AI model as the new foundation for Siri and Apple Intelligence. This collaboration is worth an estimated $1 billion annually.\n\n2. Set Apple up for life after the iPhone.\n\nOpenAI officially acquired Jony Ive\u2019s AI hardware startup, io Products, Inc., in May 2025 for approximately $6.5 billion to form its internal devices division. Despite recent shifts in focus, OpenAI (OPAI.PVT) is still expected to release its first piece of hardware with an eye toward challenging the iPhone this year. Ternus has to use his extensive hardware knowledge to think about what life after the iPhone looks like \u2014 and it needs to be more than the foldable device rumored to debut later this year.\n\n3. Reset the size of the Apple workforce in the age of AI, like others in Big Tech.\n\nBig Tech players from Oracle (ORCL) to Amazon (AMZN) to Meta (META) are firing people en masse amid pushes to adopt AI workflows. As is customary with a new CEO, Ternus may want to use his new position to resize Apple's workforce and reallocate those savings to growth investments or shareholder-friendly actions. Doing so would give Ternus an early win with shareholders and Wall Street, even though the headlines wouldn't look good. Apple is estimated to have 80,000 workers in the US and more than 160,000 globally.\n\n4. Decide if Apple wants to put more gas on content ambitions to challenge Amazon and Netflix \u2014 or pull back.\n\nApple has spent an estimated $25 billion to $30 billion on original content for Apple TV+ since its 2019 debut. That's a lot of money for not a lot of hits, other than, say, The Morning Show with Jennifer Aniston and Reese Witherspoon and the F1 movie with Brad Pitt. Ternus has to figure out if Apple wants to go all in on content like Netflix (NFLX) and Amazon (AMZN).\n\n5. Refresh the Apple management team.\n\nIt's standard practice for any incoming CEO. I suspect he has his preferred management team written up on a doc.\n\n6. Befriend President Trump as Tim Cook did.\n\nTim Cook has conducted a masterclass in working with the unpredictable Trump. Ternus cannot waste time talking to Trump and investing time in building that relationship.\n\n7. Meet Berkshire Hathaway CEO, Greg Abel.\n\nBerkshire Hathaway (BRK-B) \u2014 now led by Greg Abel rather than Tim Cook fan Warren Buffett \u2014 holds approximately 228 million Apple shares. The stake is valued at roughly $62 billion, making it the largest single holding in Berkshire\u2019s stock portfolio by a significant margin. It will be good for Ternus to establish a strong relationship with the fellow new CEO Abel. There is nothing like having a Berkshire seal of approval, especially when times get tough.\n\nRead more about Apple's CEO transition:\n\nApple CEO Tim Cook is stepping down, to be succeeded by John Ternus\n\nEverything we know about Apple's new CEO\n\nInvestors are $4 trillion richer because of Tim Cook\n\nBrian Sozzi is Yahoo Finance's Executive Editor and a member of Yahoo Finance's editorial leadership team. Follow Sozzi on X @BrianSozzi, Instagram, and LinkedIn. Tips on stories? Email brian.sozzi@yahoofinance.com.\n\nClick here for in-depth analysis of the latest stock market news and events moving stock prices\n\nRead the latest financial and business news from Yahoo Finance"}

In prepared remarks, Warsh emphasized the importance of central bank independence, warning against political encroachment.\n\n\u201cThe Fed must stay in its lane,\u201d he said, indicting that the push and pull between Trump and the Fed may be coming to an end. {"title": "Tim Cook is stepping down as Apple's CEO. Investors are $4 trillion richer because of him.", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/tim-cook-is-stepping-down-as-apples-ceo-investors-are-4-trillion-richer-because-of-him-230325543.html", "text": "Apple (AAPL) on Monday announced that CEO Tim Cook will step down from the role he\u2019s held since August 2011 on Sept. 1.\n\nCook will stay on at Apple as its executive chairman and \u201cassist with certain aspects of the company, including engaging with policymakers around the world,\u201d the company said in a statement.\n\nDuring his time as CEO, Cook oversaw the launch of a variety of new products, including the Apple Watch, AirPods, and the company\u2019s new MacBook Neo. He\u2019s also been instrumental in increasing Apple\u2019s Services segment revenue to more than $100 billion, the company\u2019s second-largest business behind the iPhone.\n\nSteve Jobs hired Cook in 1998 and promoted him to executive vice president of worldwide sales in 2002, before appointing him COO in 2005. He later took over as CEO from Jobs in 2011.\n\nDuring that time, Cook leveraged his supply chain expertise to dramatically expand Apple\u2019s business. The company\u2019s market capitalization has grown from $350 billion to just north of $4 trillion as of the end of the trading day Monday, a staggering 1,000% increase.\n\nYearly revenue has quadrupled from $108 billion in 2011 to $416 billion in 2025. Apple\u2019s iPhone revenue, in particular, has skyrocketed under Cook\u2019s leadership, from $47.1 billion to $209.6 billion this year.\n\nThe company\u2019s Apple Watch and AirPods are the world\u2019s most popular smartwatch and headphones, Apple said.\n\nImportantly, Cook pushed the company to transition from using Intel chips to power its Mac line of products to its own custom silicon, which has helped boost the performance of its laptops and desktops, allowing them to provide dramatically better battery life that competing systems are only now catching up to.\n\nAll of that has contributed to Apple\u2019s massive stock gains since Cook took over. From August 2011 to Monday, Apple stock has climbed 1,886%, easily outpacing the S&P 500\u2019s 483% gain.\n\nTernus will be stepping into the position at a time of major transition for Apple. The company is working to bring its AI capabilities up to speed after falling behind competitors such as Microsoft (MSFT) and Google (GOOG, GOOGL).\n\nIt\u2019s now expected to launch an updated version of Siri powered by Google\u2019s Gemini AI models during its WWDC conference in June.\n\nApple is also reportedly preparing its most dramatic iPhone change yet: a foldable model that the company is expected to debut shortly after Cook steps down in September.\n\nTernus will also launch Apple\u2019s rumored smart glasses, as well as any future AI-focused products meant to compete with OpenAI\u2019s planned AI-first device."}

He is a visionary whose contributions to Apple over 25 years are already too numerous to count, and he is without question the right person to lead Apple into the future. I could not be more confident in his abilities and his character, and I look forward to working closely with him on this transition and in my new role as executive chairman.\u201d\n\nReplacing Cook, who has been at Apple since Steve Jobs hired him in 1998, will be no small task.\n\nTernus, Apple\u2019s senior vice president of hardware engineering, joined Apple in 2001 and has held his current position since 2013. The 50-year-old executive graduated from the University of Pennsylvania with a degree in mechanical engineering and worked at Virtual Research Systems before moving to Apple.\n\nTernus has already made several high-profile public appearances at Apple\u2019s annual product events, including the company\u2019s latest iPhone launch and its recent MacBook Neo unveiling.\n\nHe\u2019s also the kind of perfectionist Apple is known for. During his keynote address at The University of Pennsylvania\u2019s Engineering Commencement in 2024, Ternus recounted arguing with a supplier over the number of grooves in the heads of screws that would sit in the back of his first Apple product, the Apple Cinema Display. The screws the supplier offered had 35 grooves, but Ternus demanded they stick to the 25 grooves Apple wanted.\n\n\u201cI distinctly remember stepping back for a minute and thinking to myself, \u2018What the hell am I doing? Is this normal?\u2019 And I thought about it, and I realized it might not be normal, but it's right,\u201d he said.\n\n\u201cIt's right because I'd already spent months working on that product, and if you're going to spend that much time on something, you should put in your very best effort. Maybe a customer notices, maybe they don't. But either way, whenever I saw one of those displays on someone's desk, it mattered to me to know that my teammates and I had considered everything about it.\u201d"}

The Street appears to be banking on a slow sales recovery for Target as the year stretches on.\n\nDon't forget, it has been woeful though: Target's holiday season was awful, a culmination of its heavy exposure to discretionary items and shoppers viewing its merchandise as too expensive.\n\nNot helping matters was lingering consumer angst on how Target management has handled highly publicized social issues. The retailer notched a fourth straight quarter of falling customer transactions (aka traffic). Comparable sales fell 2.5%. Walmart US saw a comp gain of 4.6%.\n\nFor the full year 2025, Target's net sales fell 1.7% to $104.8 billion, down from $106.6 billion in 2024. The decline was more pronounced in profitability, as operating income dropped 8.1% to $5.1 billion.\n\nWhat the Street is doing: Analysts have aggressively marked up their earnings estimates on Target this year and next as they bet on a turnaround, per Yahoo Finance data.\n\nBottom line: Target will enter its late May earnings release with much higher expectations around its comeback, in large part because of the stock's run-up. Target has done very little financially or operationally to justify these lofty expectations. There could be a reality check in store for the new crop of Target bulls if the retailer misses the mark."}
{"title": "Target stock is on fire in April. Here's why.", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/target-stock-is-on-fire-in-april-heres-why-210914423.html", "text": "Target's (TGT) financial performance for the past two years has been abysmal.\n\nBut its stock is up 8% in April compared to a 3.3% gain for rival Walmart (WMT), and that relative outperformance has caught my attention.\n\nHere's why Target's stock has come alive: A new note from Goldman Sachs retail analyst Kate McShane helps to explain the newfound optimism on Target.\n\n\"During our recent store checks, we have noticed a few in-store changes, including an updated baby area and larger Threshold display. Per management, these are some of the bigger changes, particularly in baby, while in 2Q, we should expect to see more changes in home, primarily from an assortment perspective, along with some Threshold shop-in-shops,\" McShane said.\n\n\"Management explained that each week and quarter, the customer should feel the level of newness and change turn up slightly, noting there will not be one month where the store feels completely different.\"\n\nPut simply, Target under new CEO Michael Fiddelke is trying to better cater to its customers' needs, creating easier-to-shop stores and lowering prices. The Street appears to be banking on a slow sales recovery for Target as the year stretches on.\n\nDon't forget, it has been woeful though: Target's holiday season was awful, a culmination of its heavy exposure to discretionary items and shoppers viewing its merchandise as too expensive.\n\nNot helping matters was lingering consumer angst on how Target management has handled highly publicized social issues. The retailer notched a fourth straight quarter of falling customer transactions (aka traffic). Comparable sales fell 2.5%. Walmart US saw a comp gain of 4.6%.\n\nFor the full year 2025, Target's net sales fell 1.7% to $104.8 billion, down from $106.6 billion in 2024. {"title": "Georgia's film boom made 75,000 jobs possible \u2014 now Marvel's exit is stripping workers of health insurance", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/georgias-film-boom-made-75-210500598.html", "text": "For more than a decade, Georgia wasn't just a filming location for Marvel \u2014 it was practically its home base.\n\nOnce a cornerstone of Atlanta's booming production economy, Marvel Studios helped turn the state into \"Hollywood of the South,\" drawn by generous tax credits, experienced crew, and some of the largest soundstages in North America.\n\nMust Read\n\nThanks to Jeff Bezos, you can now become a landlord for as little as $100 \u2014 and no, you don't have to deal with tenants or fix freezers. Here's how\n\nRobert Kiyosaki says this 1 asset will surge 400% in a year and begs investors not to miss this \u2018explosion\u2019\n\nDave Ramsey warns nearly 50% of Americans are making 1 big Social Security mistake \u2014 here\u2019s how to fix it ASAP\n\nIn recent years, however, Marvel has increasingly shifted its productions to the U.K. (1), moving away from Georgia as a primary filming base.\n\nAt its peak, the state's film industry supported more than 75,000 jobs (2) and generated more than $4.4 billion in annual production spending in 2022, according to state industry data (3) \u2014 making it one of the largest production hubs in North America, second only to California in some rankings (4).\n\nBut that boom is winding down, and the impact is increasingly felt not just in production volumes, but in something more fundamental \u2014 healthcare.\n\nWhen film work stopped meaning stable healthcare\n\nFor years, Georgia's production surge created an uncommon kind of stability in an otherwise freelance- and contract-heavy industry.\n\nMore than 400 productions were active in a single year (2), creating overlapping schedules that let crew members move from one project to the next with little downtime.\n\nIn the U.S. entertainment industry, healthcare access is closely tied to work hours and earnings thresholds. Under major union plans, such as those covering film and television workers, eligibility for health insurance depends on meeting minimum annual earnings requirements.\n\nFor example, under plans like the SAG-AFTRA Health Plan (5), workers typically need to earn at least $28,090 (the 2026 threshold) in covered income to qualify. Essentially, that means piecing together enough work across multiple productions \u2014 not relying on a single employer.\n\nWhen work is steady, coverage tends to follow. When it slows, the safety net starts to tear.\n\nBy the most recent fiscal year (2025) (1), Georgia's production spending had fallen to roughly $2.3 billion \u2014 nearly half its 2022 peak. The number of productions has also dropped sharply, from more than 400 to the mid-200s.\n\nThat drop doesn't just mean fewer jobs; it also makes it harder for workers to hit the thresholds needed to keep their health insurance.\n\nCrew members who once moved from one Marvel production to the next are now facing longer gaps between gigs. Soundstages are sitting idle, and smaller vendors are seeing less consistent work.\n\nThe result isn't just a smaller workforce \u2014 it's a more fragmented one, where healthcare coverage depends on increasingly unpredictable schedules.\n\nRead More: This $1B private real estate fund is now accessible to non-millionaires. Start investing with just $10\n\nWhy 'Hollywood of the South' started to unravel\n\nThe slowdown didn't come from a single decision. It was driven by overlapping forces across the industry.\n\nThe 2023 writers' and actors' strikes shut down much of the U.S. film industry for months, creating an estimated (6) $6 billion or more in lost wages and economic activity across production-heavy states, including Georgia.\n\nHundreds of projects were delayed or paused, cutting off the steady flow of work crews rely on. But the shift was already underway before the strikes.\n\nGlobal film production had already moved away from its post-pandemic peak. Worldwide box office sales reached about $33.9 billion in 2023, down from $42.3 billion in 2019, reflecting slower recovery (7) and more selective greenlighting by studios.\n\nThat shift has reduced the total number of production days available \u2014 a significant change for workers paid gig to gig.\n\nInside the Walt Disney Company \u2014 Marvel's parent company \u2014 that shift was structural. The studio has reduced its output (8) and has increasingly relied on contractor-based labor. Rather than maintaining large permanent teams, production crews are assembled on a project-by-project basis.\n\nThat model reflects a broader reality in the industry. Estimates vary, but industry data (9) suggests roughly 55% of U.S. film workers are freelance- or contract-based nationally.\n\nThat change has had a significant impact on healthcare stability.\n\nContract-based work typically does not guarantee continuous eligibility for employer-linked benefits. Instead, workers must accumulate enough qualifying hours across scattered projects \u2014 something that becomes harder as production volume declines.\n\nA different kind of film economy\n\nMarvel has increasingly anchored its production in the U.K., where a different labor model changes the equation \u2014 including a publicly funded healthcare system that isn't tied to employment in the same way.\n\nIn large-scale filmmaking, where productions frequently exceed hundreds of millions of dollars, labor and benefits costs are significant. Even incremental savings in healthcare obligations can influence where a production is located.\n\nWhile Georgia offers tax incentives and infrastructure, the U.K. offers a system where healthcare costs are no longer tied directly to employers.\n\nAs studios look to cut costs and reduce risk, that distinction is becoming increasingly significant. Incentives alone are no longer enough to offset broader shifts in how the industry operates.\n\nReduced production volume, contractor-based hiring, and more fragmented access to healthcare are reshaping the labor market that once powered the state's boom.\n\nAnd for Georgia's film economy, the bigger shift is not just that Marvel is pulling back. It's that the model that once supported long-term work \u2014 and the healthcare stability tied to it \u2014 is no longer the default.\n\nThe boom didn't just bust. It redefined what stability in the film industry looks like.\n\nYou May Also Like\n\nTaxes are going to change for retirees under Trump\u2019s \u2018big beautiful bill\u2019 \u2014 here are 4 reasons you can\u2019t afford to waste time\n\nRobert Kiyosaki issues grim warning for baby boomers: many could be \u2018wiped out\u2019 and homeless \u2018all over\u2019 the country\n\nVanguard\u2019s outlook on U.S. stocks is raising alarm bells for retirees. Here\u2019s why and how to protect yourself\n\nMillionaires under 43 are reshaping investing \u2014 just 25% of their portfolios are in stocks. Here\u2019s where their money is going\n\nJoin 250,000+ readers and get Moneywise\u2019s best stories and exclusive interviews first \u2014 clear insights curated and delivered weekly. It is provided without warranty of any kind."}

{"title": "Central bank independence in focus as Fed chair nominee Kevin Warsh faces confirmation hearing", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/central-bank-independence-in-focus-as-fed-chair-nominee-kevin-warsh-faces-confirmation-hearing-112647540.html", "text": "Kevin Warsh, President Trump\u2019s nominee to be the next chair of the Federal Reserve, is finally set to have his confirmation hearing on Tuesday in Washington.\n\nFront and center will be the central bank's independence. Warsh\u2019s responses to senators\u2019 questions on Fed independence, in the wake of a year of unrelenting pressure from President Trump to lower interest rates, are likely to be more consequential than any policy decision facing the central bank.\n\nThe hearing, before the Senate Banking Committee, arrives less than a month before current Fed Chair Jerome Powell\u2019s term expires on May 15.\n\nBut as things stand now, there is no clear pathway to Warsh\u2019s confirmation.\n\nRepublican Senator Thom Tillis, who sits on the banking committee and favors Warsh as a nominee, has vowed to block the confirmation until a Justice Department investigation into Powell is resolved.\n\nThe department opened a criminal probe in January into whether Powell lied to Congress in testimony last summer about cost overruns on renovations at the Fed headquarters in Washington. Powell pushed back publicly with a video statement, asserting that the Trump administration was investigating him because it disagreed with the central bank's interest-rate policy. President Trump has repeatedly hammered Powell to lower rates.\n\nRead more: How much control does the president have over the Fed and interest rates?\n\nA federal judge last month threw out two subpoenas the Justice Department issued to the Fed, effectively invalidating the criminal probe. US Attorney Jeanine Pirro has vowed to appeal, and last week, prosecutors from her office visited the Fed\u2019s headquarters unannounced but were turned away, several outlets reported.\n\nWithout Tillis\u2019s support, Warsh\u2019s nomination can\u2019t move forward. Without Tillis, there are not enough votes on the committee to advance the nomination. All 11 Democrats on the banking committee are expected to vote no.\n\nHenrietta Treyz, director of economic policy at Veda Partners, told Yahoo Finance she recently spent time with Tillis and thinks it\u2019s \u201cextraordinarily unlikely\u201d that he will back down.\n\n\u201cHe is very happy to stand up for financial freedom and the independence of the Federal Reserve,\u201d she said. \u201cAnd I think it is a real internal belief that he has that this is really critically important.\u201d\n\nFinancial questions\n\nSenate Democrats are expected to press Warsh over what they perceive as a lack of clear financial disclosures, noting that without transparent information on his holdings there\u2019s no way for the public to have confidence that he\u2019ll make decisions in the best interest of the economy.\n\nThe Office of Government Ethics last week posted records documenting Warsh\u2019s financial assets worth in excess of $100 million, including stakes in Elon Musk\u2019s SpaceX and prediction-market Polymarket. Also listed are two funds called the \u201cJuggernaut Fund,\u201d each worth more than $50 million, that do not disclose underlying assets due to pre-existing confidentiality agreements. Democrats are expected to press for those underlying assets.\n\nLast week they sent a letter to Chairman Tim Scott (R-SC) calling for the delay of any nomination proceedings until the investigations into Powell and Governor Lisa Cook, who was fired by Trump last August and is awaiting a Supreme Court ruling in the matter, are closed. They called for the committee to instead hold a public hearing to assess President Trump\u2019s involvement in directing these criminal investigations.\n\nSen. Elizabeth Warren said she still has \u201cdeep concerns that if [Warsh] is confirmed, he will be Donald Trump's sock puppet.\u201d\n\nA hawk turned dove? Where Warsh stands now\n\nIf confirmed, Warsh will inherit a difficult situation where both sides of the Fed\u2019s mandate are in conflict. Inflation has been running above the Fed\u2019s 2% target for five years, while the job market also shows signs of weakness.\n\nRead more: How jobs, inflation, and the Fed are all related\n\n\u201cWarsh will have to earn market trust and credibility around his commitment to achieving the inflation target; bona fides that always need to be earned by an incoming chair,\u201d Deutsche Bank chief economist Matt Luzzetti said. \u201cThe requirement could be more acute in the current context, with inflation well above target for five years, another price shock from the recent surge in oil prices, and the President\u2019s calls for steep Fed rate cuts.\u201d\n\nIn comments before he was nominated earlier this year, Warsh was highly critical of the Fed, saying that the central bank should \u201cdiscard its forecast of stagflation\u201d and arguing that it is overlooking that AI will be a \u201csignificant\u201d force that will boost productivity and push down inflation. Warsh argued those factors could allow the Fed to cut rates.\n\nHe has criticized Powell personally for making \u201cunwise choices,\u201d such as missing the persistence of post-pandemic inflation. Warsh has said he rejects the belief that inflation is caused by the economy growing too fast and workers getting paid too much. Rather, he argues inflation is caused by the government spending too much and printing too much money.\n\nWarsh was a Fed governor from 2006 to 2011, and at the time, he was the youngest governor in the central bank\u2019s history. Before the Fed, Warsh served as special assistant to the president for economic policy and executive secretary of the White House National Economic Council. He currently serves as the Shepard Family Distinguished Visiting Fellow in Economics at the Hoover Institution.\n\nHe owns financial assets worth in excess of $100 million, according to government disclosures, including stakes in Elon Musk\u2019s SpaceX and prediction market Polymarket. (Disclosure: Yahoo Finance has a partnership with Polymarket.)\n\nWarsh\u2019s speeches during his time as Fed governor and transcripts of policy meetings reveal he routinely raised concerns about inflation and protecting central bank credibility by ensuring inflation expectations remain anchored, even as he voted most of his tenure at the central bank to either hold rates steady or lower them.\n\nDuring his time on the Fed from February 2006 to March 2011, he voted in line with the committee consensus every time and never dissented.\n\nThe question now is whether Warsh\u2019s views have changed in light of new geopolitical developments or whether he will argue for near-term rate cuts.\n\n\u201cIf Warsh is going to lead a committee that is increasingly supportive of keeping rates steady, he might resist arguing too forcefully for rate cuts in the near-term,\u201d Luzzetti said. \u201cThe nuance for Warsh will be how he balances a desire to lower rates over time with an economic backdrop that does not call for rate cuts at present.\u201d\n\nWarsh is also expected to be asked about his current views on monetary policy. To that, Luzzetti said Warsh can discuss temporary inflation risks that require vigilance for a short period before resuming policy easing.\n\nWhile Warsh has his own views and, as chair, will need to build a consensus, there are 18 other members of a very divided FOMC whom he will have to convince.\n\nJennifer Schonberger is a veteran financial journalist covering markets, the economy, and investing. At Yahoo Finance she covers the Federal Reserve, Congress, the White House, the Treasury, the SEC, the economy, cryptocurrencies, and the intersection of Washington policy with finance. Follow her on X @Jenniferisms and on Instagram.\n\nClick here for the latest economic news and indicators to help inform your investing decisions\n\nRead the latest financial and business news from Yahoo Finance"}

He currently serves as the Shepard Family Distinguished Visiting Fellow in Economics at the Hoover Institution.\n\nHe owns financial assets worth in excess of $100 million, according to government disclosures, including stakes in Elon Musk\u2019s SpaceX and prediction market Polymarket. (Disclosure: Yahoo Finance has a partnership with Polymarket.)\n\nWarsh\u2019s speeches during his time as Fed governor and transcripts of policy meetings reveal he routinely raised concerns about inflation and protecting central bank credibility by ensuring inflation expectations remain anchored, even as he voted most of his tenure at the central bank to either hold rates steady or lower them.\n\nDuring his time on the Fed from February 2006 to March 2011, he voted in line with the committee consensus every time and never dissented.\n\nThe question now is whether Warsh\u2019s views have changed in light of new geopolitical developments or whether he will argue for near-term rate cuts.\n\n\u201cIf Warsh is going to lead a committee that is increasingly supportive of keeping rates steady, he might resist arguing too forcefully for rate cuts in the near-term,\u201d Luzzetti said. \u201cThe nuance for Warsh will be how he balances a desire to lower rates over time with an economic backdrop that does not call for rate cuts at present.\u201d\n\nWarsh is also expected to be asked about his current views on monetary policy. To that, Luzzetti said Warsh can discuss temporary inflation risks that require vigilance for a short period before resuming policy easing.\n\nWhile Warsh has his own views and, as chair, will need to build a consensus, there are 18 other members of a very divided FOMC whom he will have to convince.\n\nJennifer Schonberger is a veteran financial journalist covering markets, the economy, and investing. At Yahoo Finance she covers the Federal Reserve, Congress, the White House, the Treasury, the SEC, the economy, cryptocurrencies, and the intersection of Washington policy with finance. Follow her on X @Jenniferisms and on Instagram.\n\nClick here for the latest economic news and indicators to help inform your investing decisions\n\nRead the latest financial and business news from Yahoo Finance"}
{"title": "A UFC \u2018arena\u2019 is being built on the White House lawn for Trump's 80th birthday. It\u2019s costing $60M \u2014 $700K just for grass", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/ufc-arena-being-built-white-210000149.html", "text": "President Donald Trump told reporters last week that the UFC is going to build \"a 4,500-seat arena\" on the south lawn of the White House in preparation for its Freedom 250 card celebrating America's semiquincentennial (1).\n\nAnd while his comment conjures images of bulldozers getting ready to rumble onto the White House grounds, renderings released by the UFC paint a different picture.\n\nMust Read\n\nThanks to Jeff Bezos, you can now become a landlord for as little as $100 \u2014 and no, you don't have to deal with tenants or fix freezers. Here's how\n\nRobert Kiyosaki says this 1 asset will surge 400% in a year and begs investors not to miss this \u2018explosion\u2019\n\nDave Ramsey warns nearly 50% of Americans are making 1 big Social Security mistake \u2014 here\u2019s how to fix it ASAP\n\nOne such image (2) of the venue for the June 14 fight card \u2014 which is also Trump's 80th birthday \u2014 shows a UFC octagon surrounded by bleachers, with four arches supporting a small roof overhead and the White House in the immediate background.\n\nThat rendering \u2014 a canopy, more accurately, rather than an arena \u2014 reflects what UFC President Dana White described to The Sports Business Journal, saying, \"The only thing I want to see is the White House in the backdrop and the Washington Monument on the other side (3).\"\n\nMost fans, however, won't have access to the bleachers around the octagon, which are expected to hold about 5,000 people, including military veterans (4). Instead, 80,000 spectators can watch the event via giant screens set up at The Ellipse park, directly south of the White House (5).\n\nStill, while not exactly an arena, staging the UFC event is expected to cost a fortune.\n\nThe cost of a White House fight night\n\nMark Shapiro, president of TKO, UFC's parent company, noted that producing the card, including fighter pay and related fan fest events, is likely to run at least $60 million (6).\n\nHe added that the price is \"definitely not moving south \u2014 it could move north,\" but that TKO hopes to offset $30 million of that via partnership deals related to the event.\n\nPart of that cost includes the $700,000 that White said the company would need to repair the south lawn following the fights (7).\n\nWhite also told The Pat McAfee Show that they're building the structure in Europe before shipping it to Philadelphia and then driving it to Washington to construct on the south lawn for the fight card (8).\n\nHowever, the UFC president made it clear that TKO is footing the bill, adding, \"Not one dollar of taxpayer money will go into this (9).\" And Shapiro noted that \"We will not profit from the White House event independently (10).\"\n\nWhen comparing the event to the $20 million card UFC put on at the Sphere in 2024, White added, \"We're going to make the Sphere look like f\u2014ing ashtray money (11).\"\n\nNot everyone, though, is buying the hype. Former UFC fighter \"Filthy\" Tom Lawlor posted \"LOL that's it?\" on social media after the card \u2014 headlined by a lightweight championship and interim heavyweight title bout \u2014 was revealed (12).\n\nIn fact, many have noted the absence of mainstream stars, including Conor McGregor, Jon Jones and Ronda Rousey \u2014 the latter of which dubbed the event an \"oligarch shmooze fest\" ahead of her own May 16 fight against Gina Carano for Jake Paul's MVP promotion (13).\n\nOthers have called the event \"authoritarian theatre,\" while UFC fighter Brandon \"Raw Dawg\" Royval likened it to a Hunger Games-style event for \"billionaires and rich people\" who don't care about him (14). He added that \"I'm too Mexican-looking,\" saying that ICE \"is suspiciously arresting\" people and that \"Next thing you know, I'm in Mexico and I don't speak Spanish.\"\n\nRead More: This $1B private real estate fund is now accessible to non-millionaires. Start investing with just $10\n\nMaking White House history\n\nTrump, meanwhile, is predictably excited about the event, saying in his comments to reporters that \"I've been involved with a lot of big events\" but that \"I've never had an event that's had more interest than the UFC fight that we have right at the front door (15).\"\n\nIn the 1980s, his Trump Plaza Hotel and Casino hosted numerous high-profile combat sports events, including multiple Mike Tyson boxing matches and WrestleManias IV and V, in 1988 and 1989 respectively.\n\nAnd while past presidents have installed sporting structures \u2014 like Teddy Roosevelt's tennis court, Dwight Eisenhower's putting green or Barack Obama's basketball court (16) \u2014 at the White House, UFC 250 will mark the first ever major sporting event held on the grounds (17).\n\nThe only other competitive sport played at the White House took place thanks to President George W. Bush's White House Tee Ball Initiative, which saw little league teams play a game on the south lawn every year between 2001 and 2008 (18).\n\nYou May Also Like\n\nTaxes are going to change for retirees under Trump\u2019s \u2018big beautiful bill\u2019 \u2014 here are 4 reasons you can\u2019t afford to waste time\n\nRobert Kiyosaki issues grim warning for baby boomers: many could be \u2018wiped out\u2019 and homeless \u2018all over\u2019 the country\n\nVanguard\u2019s outlook on U.S. stocks is raising alarm bells for retirees. {"title": "Your choice of state can almost triple your tax burden. Do you know what your home base is costing you?", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/choice-state-almost-triple-tax-203000381.html", "text": "Where you live can have a major impact on your finances \u2014 and not just because of housing costs or salaries.\n\nFederal taxes are consistent across the country, but state and local taxes, including income, property, sales and excise, vary widely, and the difference isn't trivial.\n\nMust Read\n\nThanks to Jeff Bezos, you can now become a landlord for as little as $100 \u2014 and no, you don't have to deal with tenants or fix freezers. Here's how\n\nRobert Kiyosaki says this 1 asset will surge 400% in a year and begs investors not to miss this \u2018explosion\u2019\n\nDave Ramsey warns nearly 50% of Americans are making 1 big Social Security mistake \u2014 here\u2019s how to fix it ASAP\n\nIn one state, residents pay more than 13% of their incomes in taxes, while in another, it's less than 5%. That's according to recent WalletHub analysis, which, drawing on data from the Tax Policy Center, ranked all 50 states based on how much of their inhabitants' income goes to taxes (1).\n\nHere are the five states with the highest and lowest taxes in America.\n\nThe 5 states with the highest tax burden\n\nHawaii (13.3%) In Hawaii, residents pay more than 13% of their income in taxes. The biggest driver is sales and excise taxes, which alone account for nearly 7.5% of income \u2014 the highest in the nation. Add in property taxes and the country's seventh-highest income tax burden, and the Aloha State becomes the most expensive from a tax perspective.\n\nNew York (12.4%) New York's income tax burden is the second-highest in the nation, swallowing up about 4.65% of residents' income, while, at 4.22%, its property tax burden is the country's fourth-highest.\n\nVermont (11.1%) Vermont has the highest property tax burden in the U.S., at nearly 4.9% of income. Its income and sales tax burdens, meanwhile, rank 14th and 26th in the country, respectively.\n\nNew Mexico (10.8%) New Mexico's place in the top four is driven by its sales and excise tax burden, which, at 6.28% of income, is the third-highest in the country.\n\nMaine (10.0%) Maine's above-average property and income taxes push it into the top five. Its property tax burden ranks fifth at 3.95%, while its income tax burden of 2.71% ranks 15th.\n\nThe 5 states with the lowest tax burden\n\nAlaska (4.9%) Alaska has the lowest tax burden in the country. Residents pay no state income tax, and, at 1.60%, its sales and excise tax burden is among the lowest nationwide. That keeps its overall burden under 5%, despite a relatively high property tax burden of 3.32%.\n\nNew Hampshire (5.4%) New Hampshire has the lowest sales and excise tax burden in the country, along with a very low income tax burden of just 0.13%. However, it relies more heavily on property taxes, which are among the highest in the nation (2).\n\nTennessee (6.2%) Tennessee also doesn't levy an income tax on residents and has one of the lowest property tax burdens. However, a sales tax burden of 4.61% partially offsets those savings.\n\nFlorida (6.3%) Florida's lack of a state income tax is a major draw for residents and retirees. Property and sales taxes still apply, but the absence of income tax keeps the overall burden among the lowest.\n\nDelaware (6.3%) Delaware benefits from having the second-lowest sales tax burden and fourth-lowest property tax burden, although this is partly offset by an income tax burden of 3.62%, which is the third-highest in the country.\n\nYour state could be costing you thousands more\n\nBased on WalletHub's numbers, a household spending around $25,000 a year on taxable goods could pay roughly $1,600 less in sales taxes living in Delaware compared to Hawaii.\n\nRead More: This $1B private real estate fund is now accessible to non-millionaires. Start investing with just $10\n\nMeanwhile, according to Smartasset's income tax calculator, before considering deductions and credits, a single person earning $100,000 could pay about $4,892 more in state income taxes in New York than in a state with no additional income tax, such as Alaska or Tennessee.\n\nProperty taxes can make an even bigger difference. According to Smartasset's property tax calculator, on a $350,000 home, a homeowner in Vermont could pay around $6,913 a year in property taxes, compared to roughly $1,068 in Alabama (3). And that's on the same home value. In reality, median home prices are often lower in low property tax states, which can widen the gap further (4).\n\nHigher earners may feel income taxes most, while homeowners in expensive markets are more exposed to property taxes. Sales taxes, meanwhile, tend to hit those who spend more in-state, particularly on non-essential goods.\n\nBut that doesn't necessarily mean people should automatically prioritize low-tax states. Higher-tax states often use that revenue to fund public services like infrastructure, health care and education.\n\nLower-tax states, conversely, may offer fewer services or shift the burden elsewhere.\n\nYou May Also Like\n\nTaxes are going to change for retirees under Trump\u2019s \u2018big beautiful bill\u2019 \u2014 here are 4 reasons you can\u2019t afford to waste time\n\nRobert Kiyosaki issues grim warning for baby boomers: many could be \u2018wiped out\u2019 and homeless \u2018all over\u2019 the country\n\nVanguard\u2019s outlook on U.S. stocks is raising alarm bells for retirees. Here\u2019s why and how to protect yourself\n\nMillionaires under 43 are reshaping investing \u2014 just 25% of their portfolios are in stocks. Here\u2019s where their money is going\n\nJoin 250,000+ readers and get Moneywise\u2019s best stories and exclusive interviews first \u2014 clear insights curated and delivered weekly. {"title": "United Q1 earnings preview: Crude surge, premium push, and merger chatter are on the agenda", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/united-q1-earnings-preview-crude-surge-premium-push-and-merger-chatter-are-on-the-agenda-200241320.html", "text": "United Airlines (UAL) will report first quarter earnings after the bell on Tuesday, capping off a stretch that whipsawed the sector and the airline on oil prices, merger talk, and broader questions about the health of the consumer.\n\nChicago-based United is expected to report Q1 revenue of $14.45 billion, per Bloomberg consensus, up 9.4% from a year earlier. CEO Scott Kirby said last year that he expects 2026 to continue the \"revenue momentum\" for the airline.\n\nUnited is expected to post adjusted EPS of $1.09, up nearly 19.8% year over year, with EBITDA of $1.35 billion.\n\nSurging oil prices have hit airlines hard, with little relief from the on-again, off-again nature of the Strait of Hormuz closure and whether a ceasefire can be extended in the US-Israeli war with Iran.\n\nRead more: Live coverage of corporate earnings\n\nLast month, Kirby flagged $400 million in additional costs due to rising jet fuel prices, with the airline taking a potential big hit as its fuel costs are unhedged.\n\nUnited's results are expected to deflect high fuel prices as a result of its higher-end customers. In Q4, premium revenue climbed 9% year over year and 11% for the full year, outpacing overall revenue growth of 3.5%. The company expanded its premium offerings to a record 27.4 million premium seats in 2025, roughly 12% of all flown seats \u2014 and it keeps going upmarket.\n\nLast month, United unveiled the \"Relax Row,\u201d a first-of-its-kind in North America economy concept that converts three coach seats into a lie-flat, couch-like surface on long-haul widebody flights. Debuting next year, the product is positioned between United Economy and Premium Plus \u2014 an attempt to pull price-sensitive families and couples up the fare ladder without the first-class Polaris price tag.\n\nKirby and United are reportedly looking at other forms of growth. Earlier this month, reports surfaced that Kirby had pitched a potential tie-up with American Airlines (AAL) directly to the Trump administration during a February White House meeting, framing it as a \"National Champion\" strategy to take on subsidized foreign carriers.\n\nAmerican publicly rejected the chatter on April 17, saying it is \"not engaged with or interested\" in any merger talks and warning such a deal would be bad for competition.\n\nAnalysts will press Kirby on American or whether JetBlue or another target is in play. United\u2019s bitter rival, Delta (DAL), had its CEO predict more airlines would merge due to fuel costs and uncertainty, with some even going out of business."}
{"title": "United Q1 earnings preview: Crude surge, premium push, and merger chatter are on the agenda", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/united-q1-earnings-preview-crude-surge-premium-push-and-merger-chatter-are-on-the-agenda-200241320.html", "text": "United Airlines (UAL) will report first quarter earnings after the bell on Tuesday, capping off a stretch that whipsawed the sector and the airline on oil prices, merger talk, and broader questions about the health of the consumer.\n\nChicago-based United is expected to report Q1 revenue of $14.45 billion, per Bloomberg consensus, up 9.4% from a year earlier. CEO Scott Kirby said last year that he expects 2026 to continue the \"revenue momentum\" for the airline.\n\nUnited is expected to post adjusted EPS of $1.09, up nearly 19.8% year over year, with EBITDA of $1.35 billion.\n\nSurging oil prices have hit airlines hard, with little relief from the on-again, off-again nature of the Strait of Hormuz closure and whether a ceasefire can be extended in the US-Israeli war with Iran.\n\nRead more: Live coverage of corporate earnings\n\nLast month, Kirby flagged $400 million in additional costs due to rising jet fuel prices, with the airline taking a potential big hit as its fuel costs are unhedged.\n\nUnited's results are expected to deflect high fuel prices as a result of its higher-end customers. In Q4, premium revenue climbed 9% year over year and 11% for the full year, outpacing overall revenue growth of 3.5%. The company expanded its premium offerings to a record 27.4 million premium seats in 2025, roughly 12% of all flown seats \u2014 and it keeps going upmarket.\n\nLast month, United unveiled the \"Relax Row,\u201d a first-of-its-kind in North America economy concept that converts three coach seats into a lie-flat, couch-like surface on long-haul widebody flights. Debuting next year, the product is positioned between United Economy and Premium Plus \u2014 an attempt to pull price-sensitive families and couples up the fare ladder without the first-class Polaris price tag.\n\nKirby and United are reportedly looking at other forms of growth. Earlier this month, reports surfaced that Kirby had pitched a potential tie-up with American Airlines (AAL) directly to the Trump administration during a February White House meeting, framing it as a \"National Champion\" strategy to take on subsidized foreign carriers.\n\nAmerican publicly rejected the chatter on April 17, saying it is \"not engaged with or interested\" in any merger talks and warning such a deal would be bad for competition.\n\nAnalysts will press Kirby on American or whether JetBlue or another target is in play. United\u2019s bitter rival, Delta (DAL), had its CEO predict more airlines would merge due to fuel costs and uncertainty, with some even going out of business."}
{"title": "I\u2019m in Chapter 13 bankruptcy and just got married. My payments jumped from $300 to $2,000 \u2014 did we screw up?", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/m-chapter-13-bankruptcy-just-193500492.html", "text": "Marriage is a meeting of hearts. And finances. And all that comes with it. For some, that could mean bringing great wealth, while for others, great baggage.\n\nImagine Ken and Karen, who meet in midlife, each on their second marriage \u2014 but first time getting love right. When you know you know. And when you're 50-something, there's no time to waste. So, they jumped right in.\n\nMust Read\n\nThanks to Jeff Bezos, you can now become a landlord for as little as $100 \u2014 and no, you don't have to deal with tenants or fix freezers. Here's how\n\nRobert Kiyosaki says this 1 asset will surge 400% in a year and begs investors not to miss this \u2018explosion\u2019\n\nDave Ramsey warns nearly 50% of Americans are making 1 big Social Security mistake \u2014 here\u2019s how to fix it ASAP\n\nThe problem is, Ken filed for Chapter 13 bankruptcy, so he could save his home from foreclosure. He was paying $300 per month in repayments, which was manageable on his $45,000 salary in Missouri. That was 8% of his pre-tax take-home pay. Not always easy, but doable.\n\nBut because his wife, Karen, makes $74,000, the court has increased the repayment to $2,000 a month \u2014 20% on their household pre-tax income. While Ken expected an increase, he did not foresee this.\n\nKen's got another 18 months left until it's paid off. Did he compromise their honeymoon period, or worse, their financial future?\n\nHow the court calculates Chapter 13\n\nA chapter 13 bankruptcy is also called a wage earner's plan. Once married, this takes into account the spouse and the household's financial position (1). It calculates a debtor's disposable income, as determined by the Missouri Means Test for bankruptcy (2), which Ken and Karen were above.\n\nWhile strangers on the internet tell Ken to \"just get the marriage annulled\" and get remarried once the bankruptcy is finalized, that's not what they want to do. It's also not the smartest idea to risk being perceived as gaming the system, which could cause more trouble.\n\nKen and Karen should contact a bankruptcy attorney immediately to evaluate the change in their financial situation and file a motion to change the plan. All expenses should be accounted for to make a case for a lower payment.\n\nThere are other instances (3), like a hardship discharge or a temporary suspension of payments. Switching to Chapter 7 isn't possible because Ken's income is above the means test. Ken also needs to factor in the attorney's fees, which could be costly.\n\nEither way, Ken and Karen should get all their documents in order \u2014 pay stubs, tax returns and amended financials organized \u2014 to decide if a plan modification is justified. A marriage might be scrutinized more (4), because the income boost is predictable.\n\nRead More: This $1B private real estate fund is now accessible to non-millionaires. Start investing with just $10\n\nSacrifice now for stability later\n\nThe standard, 'earn more, spend less' advice gets tricky here. The more Ken earns, the more he'll pay. The less he earns, the less he'll pay.\n\nKen would benefit from changing his perspective about this moment. It's a time to resolve his debts, not to get ahead financially. If he can knuckle down for the next 18 months, he'll be clear.\n\nThe couple might be better off redirecting those attorney fees to a financial planner and marriage counselor, to help them navigate short-term. Maybe Ken can adjust his personal spending to cover more of the additional $1,700 per month, so the financial burden falls mostly on him.\n\nOr they could view it as their first big challenge starting a long life together, and handling it as a team, knowing it's temporary.\n\nYou May Also Like\n\nTaxes are going to change for retirees under Trump\u2019s \u2018big beautiful bill\u2019 \u2014 here are 4 reasons you can\u2019t afford to waste time\n\nRobert Kiyosaki issues grim warning for baby boomers: many could be \u2018wiped out\u2019 and homeless \u2018all over\u2019 the country\n\nVanguard\u2019s outlook on U.S. stocks is raising alarm bells for retirees. {"title": "Why gas prices above $3 per gallon are predicted for the rest of the year \u2014 even if Iran peace talks succeed", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/why-gas-prices-above-3-per-gallon-are-predicted-for-the-rest-of-the-year--even-if-iran-peace-talks-succeed-183024836.html", "text": "Energy observers are increasingly acknowledging a bottom line for motorists that prices at the pump are likely to be elevated for the foreseeable future \u2014 no matter what happens in the short term in the Strait of Hormuz and with another round of peace talks on tap this week.\n\n\u201cWe will probably see those high prices sticky for longer,\u201d CIBC Private Wealth senior energy trader Rebecca Babin told Yahoo Finance on Monday.\n\nShe projects that average gasoline prices will remain above $3 per gallon for all of 2026, even if the strait is fully opened by this summer.\n\nIt\u2019s a prediction shared by others, including GasBuddy\u2019s Patrick De Haan, who recently suggested that, even factoring in positive efforts to open the strait, prices will be between $3.35 and $3.95 throughout the summer months.\n\nRead more: It's not just gas prices. How the Iran war is coming for your grocery bill.\n\nEven a Trump Cabinet member acknowledged the likelihood. Energy Secretary Chris Wright said Sunday on CNN that gas below $3 per gallon \u201cmight not happen until next year,\u201d but argued that prices have peaked.\n\nThe commentary is a reality check of sorts for drivers and comes as crude oil prices and markets remain volatile around rapidly changing developments in the region, as well as upcoming talks in Pakistan, where Vice President JD Vance is set to lead the US side in another round of negotiations on Tuesday ahead of a Wednesday ceasefire deadline.\n\nPresident Trump, for his part, is downplaying gas price increases and threatening renewed escalation if the talks fail. If Iran doesn\u2019t accept a deal, he posted over the weekend, he will order the US military to \u201cknock out every single Power Plant, and every single Bridge\u201d in Iran.\n\nGas is hovering at about $4 per gallon in the US, according to the American Automobile Association, up more than a dollar from before the war.\n\nRead more: March CPI breakdown: Iran war sends gas prices skyrocketing, airfare climbing\n\n\u2018Rockets and feathers\u2019\n\nAny easing of gas price pressures is likely to be slow and unsatisfying for drivers \u2014 as well as for Republicans facing midterm voters \u2014 in part because of a historical phenomenon that economists have taken to calling \u201crockets and feathers.\u201d\n\nAs the Federal Reserve Bank of St. Louis explained in 2022, crude oil and refined gas prices don\u2019t always move in tandem. They often shoot upward together (like a rocket), but when crude oil prices later ease, refined gasoline prices sometimes drift down at a much slower rate (like a falling feather).\n\nNY Mercantile - Delayed Quote \u2022 USD\n\nBrent Crude Oil Last Day Financ (BZ=F)\n\n94.85 -0.63 (-0.66%)\n\nAs of 12:10:06 am GMT-4. Market open.\n\nBZ=F CL=F\n\nThe formal economic term for the phenomenon is \u201casymmetric pass-through,\u201d and it stems from a variety of causes, including the lag between refiners buying crude oil and then selling their refined product and the need to preemptively protect bottom lines in moments of uncertainty.\n\nWhat it means in practice is that drivers are often the last to feel relief when oil shocks ease, leading to outsized political costs. Just ask former President Joe Biden.\n\nIt was in the aftermath of Vladimir Putin\u2019s invasion of Ukraine in 2022 that both crude oil and pump prices spiked. Prices at the pump then stayed elevated even after crude oil prices eased, frustrating Biden and his team for months.\n\nThe administration began a public pressure campaign in March of that year, with then-press secretary Jen Psaki saying at one point that Biden rejected \u201cthe so-called \u2018rockets and feathers\u2019 phenomenon.\u201d\n\nBut the pressure campaign had little effect, and Biden was still focused on the issue months later, tweeting an appeal in July to stations to \u201cbring down the price you are charging.\u201d\n\nRead more: How to protect your money as Mideast turmoil fuels market volatility\n\nA likely point of frustration for Trump\n\nThe phenomenon appears likely to repeat this time around and could be amplified by the uncertain end to hostilities and by damage to oil infrastructure in the Middle East.\n\nIn her appearance on Monday, CIBC\u2019s Babin pointed to a variety of factors that could mean \u201cthe floor [for gas prices] is naturally going to reside higher, especially since I think that many countries will start to think about stockpiling more aggressively going forward.\u201d\n\nHigher prices for longer would be frustrating for Trump and his team, who have been promising a quick drop in prices since the Iran conflict began.\n\nThe president even contradicted Wright\u2019s acknowledgment that prices could stay above $3 a gallon for 2026, saying in an interview with The Hill on Monday, \u201cI think he\u2019s wrong on that. Totally wrong.\u201d\n\nBen Werschkul is a Washington correspondent for Yahoo Finance.\n\nClick here for political news related to business and money policies that will shape tomorrow's stock prices\n\nRead the latest financial and business news from Yahoo Finance"}

{"title": "'Everyone's nervous': Wells Fargo CEO on how businesses and consumers feel about the economy", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/everyones-nervous-wells-fargo-ceo-on-how-businesses-and-consumers-feel-about-the-economy-182934133.html", "text": "Wells Fargo (WFC) CEO Charles Scharf said on Monday that the US economy has been resilient, but he also acknowledged how bad sentiment is among American consumers and businesses.\n\n\u201cRight now, from everything that we see, the economy is still extremely strong,\u201d Scharf said during an interview with David Rubenstein at the Economic Club of Washington, D.C., acknowledging the wide divergence from how consumers are feeling amid uncertainty stemming from the Iran war.\n\n\u201cThey\u2019re getting through it. Businesses have gone into this in strong financial shape. So those are all the good things. But then when you ask them how they feel, everyone's nervous,\u201d Scharf said.\n\nHe also said that consumers are adjusting their spending based on higher gas prices. Altogether, he described the economic dynamic as \u201cneutral to just beginning to see some potential for some negative impacts.\u201d\n\nPresident Trump said earlier on Monday in a Bloomberg interview that he\u2019s not likely to extend the current two-week ceasefire with Iran that expires late on Wednesday. Trump said the blockade on the Strait of Hormuz, which has the world\u2019s oil market in a supply shock, would not be lifted until a deal is reached.\n\n\u201cIf the conflict ends, the straits open up, production returns in some reasonable period of time, there will be this impact on consumer spend, on some of these other things, but in that kind of environment, it won't be damaging. If this goes on for a longer period of time, it can be more damaging,\u201d he added.\n\nWells Fargo and the country\u2019s other biggest banks reported strong increases in first quarter profits last week. The San Francisco based bank and its peers showed healthy consumer spending growth range between 5% and 9% across the country\u2019s four largest banks. And on analyst calls, Scharf and other executives struck an upbeat tone, judging the US economy and consumers in aggregate as \u201cresilient.\u201d\n\nBig banks lend less heavily to lower income borrowers than small and more specialized rivals. They also judge the health of their US customers on their spending activity and the unemployment rate, which can exclude other financial pressures.\n\nThe upbeat sentiment from lenders struck a somewhat discordant pitch with how consumers feel generally. The latest University of Michigan Consumer Sentiment Index showed that US consumer confidence this month has dropped to its lowest reading in the survey's 74-year history.\n\nDuring the same interview, Scharf voiced his support for a Federal Reserve immune to external pressures, saying \u201cthe independence of the Fed is critically important\u201d when asked about the topic by Rubenstein. He also played down worries over the private credit industry, arguing that it isn\u2019t \u201cbig enough to be a systemic risk.\u201d"}

{"title": "Tesla is last in the 'Magnificent 7' rally \u2014 and the first tech giant to report earnings: Chart of the Day", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/tesla-is-last-in-the-magnificent-7-rally--and-the-first-tech-giant-to-report-earnings-chart-of-the-day-173248863.html", "text": "Tesla (TSLA) heads into earnings Wednesday night as the weakest link of the \u201cMagnificent Seven\u201d \u2014 and it\u2019s the first of the group to report.\n\nSince the broader market\u2019s March 30 low, Tesla is up only 11%, dead last among its Magnificent Seven tech peers. It\u2019s also down 12% year to date, the second-worst Mag 7 performer, with only Apple (AAPL) faring worse. And on today\u2019s tape, it\u2019s the second-biggest decliner in the group, trailing only Meta (META).\n\nThe one-year chart tells the story of a range-bound stock. Four formations stand out.\n\nFirst, a months-long sideways consolidation through the summer, with price oscillating around the 200-day moving average. Second, a steady climb that carried the stock into the fall. Third, a steep rally to new all-time highs in December that turned into a false breakout \u2014 the move was quickly reversed. And fourth, a long descending trendline that defined the decline into the April lows and that Tesla just broke above last week.\n\nOn Friday, Tesla barely closed above its 200-day, which sits around $400. Today, the stock has slipped back below it. But the 200-day is nearly flat right now, and flat moving averages are notoriously noisy.\n\nThe real test isn\u2019t the moving average. It\u2019s Wednesday\u2019s earnings report \u2014 and it doubles as the first check on whether the Magnificent Seven can keep leading the broader rally. Since the March 30 low, the group has outpaced every major index, and Tesla is first up with hard numbers.\n\nLevels to watch: Above $400, the next zone of potential resistance sits at $450 to $460, an area of prior price action. Four formations stand out.\n\nFirst, a months-long sideways consolidation through the summer, with price oscillating around the 200-day moving average. Second, a steady climb that carried the stock into the fall. Third, a steep rally to new all-time highs in December that turned into a false breakout \u2014 the move was quickly reversed. And fourth, a long descending trendline that defined the decline into the April lows and that Tesla just broke above last week.\n\nOn Friday, Tesla barely closed above its 200-day, which sits around $400. {"title": "Warsh commits to monetary policy independence, says president expressing views on rates isn't a threat", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/warsh-commits-to-monetary-policy-independence-says-president-expressing-views-on-rates-isnt-a-threat-172825788.html", "text": "Federal Reserve chair nominee Kevin Warsh will tell Senate lawmakers Tuesday that setting interest rates independently is \u201cessential,\u201d but that the president\u2019s views on monetary policy don\u2019t threaten central bank independence.\n\n\u201cLet me be clear: monetary policy independence is essential,\u201d Warsh wrote in prepared remarks. \u201cMonetary policymakers must act in the nation\u2019s interest . . . their decisions the product of analytic rigor, meaningful deliberation, and unclouded decision-making.\u201d\n\nWarsh, who will give his opening statement before the Senate Banking Committee before facing questioning, wrote that he does not believe the \u201coperational independence of monetary policy is particularly threatened when elected officials \u2014 presidents, senators, or members of the House \u2014 state their views on interest rates.\u201d\n\nBut President Trump has done far more than state his views. In speeches, press conferences, and Truth Social posts, he has demanded lower interest rates and lambasted current Chair Jerome Powell, mocking him as \u201ctoo slow,\u201d \u201ctoo late,\u201d \u201cincompetent,\u201d and \u201ccrooked.\u201d\n\nRead more: How much control does the president have over the Fed and interest rates?\n\nHis Justice Department opened a criminal inquiry into whether Powell lied to Congress about renovation costs at the Fed headquarters, a move Powell said was designed to pressure the central bank to lower rates.\n\nIn his prepared remarks, Warsh says he believes central bankers must be strong enough to listen to a diversity of views, but that Fed independence is largely up to the Fed.\n\nWarsh, 56, was a Fed governor from 2006 to 2011 and earlier served as special assistant to the president for economic policy and executive secretary of the White House National Economic Council. He is currently a visiting fellow in economics at the Hoover Institution, a conservative think tank.\n\nMum on interest rates\n\nLargely absent from Warsh\u2019s opening testimony is any mention of his current views on monetary policy. A review of his speeches during his Fed tenure and transcripts of policy meetings paints a picture of an inflation hawk by philosophy but a data-driven practitioner. As a governor on the Federal Open Market Committee, Warsh joined the committee's consensus on every vote and never dissented. That included three rate hikes when he first came on in 2006.\n\nMore recently, Warsh has advocated lower interest rates, arguing that the Fed should \"discard its forecast of stagflation\" and predicting that AI will be a \"significant\" force that boosts productivity and lowers inflation, allowing for lower rates.\n\nIn his testimony, Warsh noted Congress tasked the Fed with the mission to ensure price stability \u201cwithout excuse or equivocation, argument or anguish.\u201d He wrote, however, that inflation is a choice and the Fed needs to take responsibility for it, calling low inflation the Fed\u2019s plot armor. Warsh warned that when inflation surges, it hurts the least well-off and erodes purchasing power.\n\nRead more: How the Fed rate decision affects your bank accounts, loans, credit cards, and investments\n\nHowever, he argued Fed independence pertains to monetary policy and that the central bank isn\u2019t entitled to the same independence on bank regulations or other matters. He argued that the Fed needs to \u201cstay in its lane\u201d and that Fed independence is put at greater risk when it strays into fiscal or social policy.\n\n\u201cI believe that monetary policy independence is earned \u2014 and better policy decisions crafted \u2014 by steering clear of distractions,\u201d he said. \u201cI favor a clearer, cleaner match between the Fed\u2019s powers and responsibilities.\u201d\n\nWarsh said that this is a time of \u201cgreat consequence\u201d for the US economy, calling it perhaps the most significant hinge point in a couple of generations.\n\n\u201cI am committed to ensuring that the conduct of monetary policy remains strictly independent,\u201d said Warsh. \u201cI am equally committed to working with the Administration and Congress on non-monetary matters that are part of the Fed\u2019s remit. And I commit to accountability in all the Fed\u2019s functions.\u201d\n\nJennifer Schonberger is a veteran financial journalist covering markets, the economy, and investing. At Yahoo Finance she covers the Federal Reserve, Congress, the White House, the Treasury, the SEC, the economy, cryptocurrencies, and the intersection of Washington policy with finance. Follow her on X @Jenniferisms and on Instagram.\n\nClick here for the latest economic news and indicators to help inform your investing decisions\n\nRead the latest financial and business news from Yahoo Finance"}

{"title": "Workers aren't happy with their pay. But they're not looking to switch jobs, either.", "link": "https://sg.finance.yahoo.com/news/workers-arent-happy-with-their-pay-but-theyre-not-looking-to-switch-jobs-either-172151650.html", "text": "People are clinging to their jobs despite dismal feelings about wages and promotion opportunities, according to the New York Federal Reserve\u2019s latest labor market survey.\n\nIn March, survey respondents\u2019 expected likelihood of switching to a new employer hit 9.7%, the lowest level since March 2021. That tracks with government data from the month prior, which showed the number of quits as a percent of total employment at 1.9% as skittish workers try to avoid braving an uncertain job market.\n\nBut workers\u2019 reluctance to quit can also give bosses the upper hand and suppress wage competition \u2014 putting consumers in a tough spot as price increases threaten to outpace pay gains.\n\nIndeed, the New York Fed\u2019s labor market survey showed that workers\u2019 satisfaction with wage compensation plunged from 55.6% in November, when the last survey was conducted, to 52.3% in March. That was the lowest level since the New York Fed began tracking the data in March 2014.\n\nDo you have a story about navigating the job market? Reach out to Emma Ockerman here.\n\nWage satisfaction was particularly bleak for lower-income workers, with just 30.9% of those making less than $60,000 feeling decent about their current pay.\n\nOverall satisfaction with promotion opportunities, meanwhile, also hit 41.2%, another record low dating back to 2014. Women felt especially negative, with their satisfaction reaching 35.2%.\n\nFewer people say they\u2019re searching for a job compared to November, consistent with recent reports that the labor market might be stabilizing. The unemployment rate in March, at 4.3%, was an improvement from November\u2019s 4.6%.\n\nAnd some workers\u2019 reluctance to jump to a new workplace might have to do with pay, rather than just anxiety. The minimum pay respondents would need to accept another job hit a record high in March of nearly $85,000, driven by men \u2014 who wanted $26,000 more than women on average \u2014 and workers with a college degree.\n\nEmma Ockerman is a reporter covering the economy and labor for Yahoo Finance. You can reach her at emma.ockerman@yahooinc.com.\n\nSign up for the Mind Your Money newsletter\n\nClick here for the latest personal finance news to help you with investing, paying off debt, buying a home, retirement, and more"}
